When Does a Waqf Trustee Become a Traitor?
Collection of rulings on trustee betrayal from Al-Dhakhira and Al-Qunyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the acts that constitute khiyanah of a waqf trustee and explain the obligatory consequence of dismissal.

Core Idea
A waqf trustee's unauthorized sale or failure to protect waqf property constitutes khiyanah, mandating dismissal by the qadi.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq draws on earlier sources (Al-Dhakhira and Al-Qunyah) to clarify when a waqf trustee's actions amount to betrayal (khiyanah). The rulings establish that any impermissible disposition or failure to protect waqf property triggers dismissal. The text also shows how the principle extends through analogical reasoning (qiyas).

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific acts of khiyanah
Extract from the passage the three concrete examples of khiyanah: selling part of waqf land to repair the rest; failing to prevent a buyer from cutting tree trunks that were not sold; mixing waqf proceeds (oil with reeds).
These are not exhaustive; the passage ends with 'wa li yaqis ma lam yaqul' encouraging analogy.
2
Determine the consequence of khiyanah
For each act, note that the trustee becomes a traitor (kha'in) and the qadi must dismiss him ('azl). The dismissal is obligatory (wajib).
The text says 'سبيله أن يعزله' – his way is to dismiss him, indicating necessity.
3
Distinguish permissible acts from betrayal
The passage distinguishes selling mulberry leaves (permissible as produce) from selling trunks (not permissible). Recognize that the trustee may dispose of income/growth but not the corpus of the waqf.
This distinction is key: the trust is over the property, not its produce.
4
Apply the principle analogically
The phrase 'وليقلس ما لم يقل' instructs to analogize similar cases. Think of other actions that would similarly betray the trust, e.g., renting waqf property at below market rate, negligence leading to damage.
The principle: any act that violates the trustee's fiduciary duty or wastes waqf assets constitutes khiyanah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما في الذخيرة أنه لا بد من هدم المشتري البناء فإنه قال : وإذا خربت أرض الوقف وأراد القيم أن يبيع بعضها منها ليرم الباقي ليس له ذلك، فإن باعه فهو باطل، فإن هدم المشتري البناء أو صرم النخل فينبغي للقاضي أن يخرج القيم عن هذا الوقف لأنه صار خائناً، ولا ينبغي للقاضي أن يأمن الخائن بل سبيله أن يعزله .اهـ. ثم قال بعده: قرية وقف على أرباب مسمين في يد المتولي باع المتولي ورق أشجار التوت جاز لأنه بمنزلة الغلة، فلو أراد المشتري قطع قوائم الشجر يمنع لأنها ليست بمبيعة، ولو امتنع المتولي من منع المشتري عن قطع القوائم كان ذلك خيانة منه، فاستفيد منه أنه إذا لم يمنع من يتلف شيئاً للوقف كان خائناً ويعزل، وفي القنية : قيم يخلط غلة الدهن بغلة البواري فهو سارق خائن اهـ. فاستفيد منه أنه إذا تصرف بما لا يجوز كان خائناً يستحق العزل وليقس ما لم يقل
From Al-Dhakhira: The buyer must demolish the building. He said: When the land of a waqf becomes ruined and the qayyim wants to sell part of it to repair the rest, he does not have that right. If he sells it, the sale is void. If the buyer demolishes the building or cuts down the date palms, then the qadi should remove the qayyim from this waqf because he has become a traitor. It is not appropriate for the qadi to trust a traitor; rather his way is to dismiss him. Then he said afterwards: A village is a waqf for named individuals in the hand of the mutawalli. The mutawalli sold the mulberry leaves; it is permissible because it is like produce. If the buyer wanted to cut the trunks of the trees, he is prevented because they are not sold. If the mutawalli refrains from preventing the buyer from cutting the trunks, that is betrayal from him. From this it is derived that if he does not prevent someone who destroys something of the waqf, he is a traitor and is dismissed. In Al-Qunyah: A qayyim mixes the produce of oil with the produce of reeds; he is a thief and a traitor. From this it is derived that if he acts in a way that is not permissible, he is a traitor deserving dismissal, and analogize for what is not said.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a series of rulings regarding khiyanah (betrayal) of the waqf trustee. It begins by quoting Al-Dhakhira: if a trustee sells part of waqf land to repair the rest, the sale is void because it involves disposing of waqf property for other than its designated purpose. If the buyer demolishes or cuts, the trustee is deemed a traitor and must be dismissed. The second ruling: selling mulberry leaves is permissible because they are produce, but selling trunks is not. If the trustee fails to prevent the buyer from cutting trunks, he is betraying. The third ruling from Al-Qunyah: mixing proceeds of different endowments is thievery and betrayal. The general principle: any impermissible act by the trustee constitutes khiyanah warranting dismissal. The phrase 'wa li yaqis ma lam yaqul' means analogize other similar cases to these.

Key Terms
خيانة (khiyana): Betrayal of trust by the waqf trustee through impermissible actions such as selling waqf property or failing to protect it.
قيم (qayyim): The person in charge of managing a waqf, similar to mutawalli.
عزل ('azl): Dismissal of the trustee by the qadi for betrayal or other reasons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a trustee sells a part of waqf land to repair the rest?
A) It is permissible if the qadi approves
B) The sale is void and the trustee becomes a traitor
C) It is recommended to sell
D) It is valid if the proceeds are used for repair

Key Takeaway
A waqf trustee's misuse of authority or failure to protect the waqf constitutes betrayal (khiyanah), making his dismissal wajib upon the qadi.

Qadi's Option When Waqf Trustee Betrays
Taqrir on qadi's discretion in waqf betrayal cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the qadi's options when a waqf trustee's betrayal is established and explain the rationale.

Core Idea
Betrayal does not mandate dismissal; the qadi may also appoint a co-trustee.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a practical question in waqf administration: what should a qadi do when a trustee is proven untrustworthy? The answer reveals a nuanced approach focusing on the purpose of preserving the waqf, not punitive dismissal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
The passage opens with a hypothetical: if a trustee's betrayal is proven, may the qadi appoint a co-trustee without dismissal? Understand the scenario.
2
State the ruling
The answer is yes. The qadi has a choice: dismiss or co-opt a trustworthy person. The ruling is based on achieving the purpose, not a fixed penalty.
3
Locate the supporting text
The author cites Al-Qunyah, which gives an example: selling waqf property is betrayal, and the qadi may either dismiss the trustee or appoint a co-trustee.
4
Understand the rationale
The purpose of the waqf is preservation. Co-opting a trustworthy person meets that purpose while possibly retaining the trustee's experience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : إذا ثبتت خيانته هل للقاضي أن يضم إليه ثقة من غير أن يعزله؟ قلت : نعم لأن المقصود حصل بضم الثقة إليه. قال في القنية : متولي الوقف باع شيئاً منه أو أرضه فهو خيانة فيعزل أو يضم إليه ثقة اهـ
If you say: If his betrayal is established, does the qadi have the option to appoint a trustworthy person alongside him without dismissing him? I say: Yes, because the purpose is achieved by appointing a trustworthy person to him. It is stated in Al-Qunyah: The mutawalli of a waqf sells something of it or its land; that is betrayal, so he is dismissed or a trustworthy person is appointed alongside him.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This is a question-answer format (taqrir) within the commentary. The question is: when a trustee's betrayal is proven, can the qadi avoid dismissal by appointing a trustworthy co-trustee? The answer is yes, because the objective of safeguarding the waqf is achieved. The text from Al-Qunyah confirms that for betrayal (like selling waqf property), the trustee is either dismissed or a trustworthy person is appointed to supervise him. This shows that dismissal is not the only option; the qadi may choose to retain the trustee but with oversight.

Key Terms
ثقة (thiqah): A trustworthy person appointed by the qadi to oversee the betraying trustee.
ضم (damm): Appointing a trustworthy person alongside the trustee without dismissal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a trustee's betrayal is established, what option does the qadi have besides dismissal?
A) The qadi must dismiss him immediately
B) The qadi can appoint a trustworthy person to supervise him
C) The qadi can ignore the betrayal
D) The qadi must refer to the waqf founder

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi waqf law, proven betrayal gives the qadi a choice between dismissal and co-option of a trustworthy person.

Trustee's Authority to Delegate and Effect of Qadi's Appointment
Ruling from Al-Qunyah on trustee delegation and qadi's appointment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a trustee's delegation and explain why the qadi's death does not invalidate his appointment.

Core Idea
Trustee may delegate only if the qadi granted general authority; the appointment continues even if the qadi leaves office.

The management of waqf requires clear rules on delegation. This passage from Al-Qunyah, cited in Al-Bahr al-Raiq, clarifies two key points: when a trustee may appoint a deputy, and whether the trustee's authority lapses when the appointing qadi dies or is removed. Understanding these rules ensures continuity in waqf administration.

Guided Path
1
Isolate the two legal rulings
The passage contains two distinct rulings: (1) the trustee's ability to delegate, and (2) the effect of the qadi's death on the appointment. Separate them in your mind.
2
Determine the condition for delegation
The text says 'in kana al-qadi al-tafwid ilayhi' — only if the qadi gave general delegation (tafwid). This is a condition that must be met.
General delegation means the qadi appointed the trustee with broad authority, not limited to specific tasks.
3
Apply the inverse condition
If the condition is not met (no tafwid), the trustee cannot delegate. The phrase 'wa illa fala' makes this clear.
4
Analyze the continuity rule
The second ruling is unconditional: death or removal of the qadi does not affect the trustee's appointment. It remains as it is.
This ensures stability; the trustee does not need reappointment by a new qadi.
5
Reflect on the legal wisdom
The two rulings together protect the waqf: delegation is restricted to authorized cases, but the trustee's position is stable against changes in the judiciary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أحكام المتولي من القاضي ما في القنية للمتولي أن يوكل فيما فوض إليه إن القاضي التفويض إليه وإلا فلا ولو مات القاضي أو عزل يبقى ما نصبه على حاله اهـ
From the rulings of the qadi concerning the trustee is what is in Al-Qunyah: The trustee may delegate (yuwakkil) in what has been delegated to him if the qadi has delegated to him (i.e., appointed him with general authority); otherwise not. And if the qadi dies or is removed, what he appointed remains as it is.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage from Al-Qunyah, quoted in Al-Bahr al-Raiq, addresses two issues. First, the trustee has the authority to appoint a deputy (wakil) only if the qadi gave him broad delegation (tafwid). If the qadi's appointment was specific, the trustee cannot delegate. Second, the validity of the trustee's appointment is not affected by the qadi's death or removal; the trustee continues in his role. This is consistent with the rule that appointments by a judge are not automatically invalidated when the judge leaves office.

Key Terms
يوكل (yuwakkil): The trustee appoints a deputy (wakil) to act on his behalf.
فوض إليه (fawwada ilayhi): Qadi delegated broad authority to the trustee, allowing further delegation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition may the trustee delegate his duties to another?
A) Always
B) Only if the qadi died
C) Only if the qadi gave him general delegation (tafwid)
D) Only with the permission of the waqf founder

Key Takeaway
Trustee's delegation is conditioned on the qadi's general authority, but the trustee's own appointment survives the qadi's death or removal.

Qadi's Appointment of Pro Bono Nazir Over Stipulated Nazir
Ruling on qadi's authority to override stipulation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a qadi may appoint a pro bono nazir despite the waqf founder's stipulation, and explain why the appointment is valid.

Core Idea
Qadi may appoint a pro bono nazir when the stipulated nazir's trustworthiness is in doubt.

Waqf founders often stipulate a specific nazir to oversee their endowment. But what happens if that nazir's integrity becomes questionable? In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, we learn that the qadi has the authority to appoint an alternative nazir on a voluntary basis. This protects the waqf without violating the founder's intent absolutely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the waqf founder has stipulated a specific nazir, but that nazir's trustworthiness is now in doubt—either the nazir himself doubts or the qadi suspects.
2
State the ruling
The qadi's appointment of a new nazir pro bono (hissba) is valid (sahih) despite the stipulation.
3
Identify the condition
The condition for validity is doubt in the original nazir's trustworthiness; without this doubt, the appointment would not be allowed.
4
Note the authority
The ruling is based on the statement of Al-Khassaf, a Hanafi authority on waqf, indicating the source of this exception.
5
Explain the rationale
The new nazir serves pro bono (without compensation), so the waqf is not financially burdened. This balances the founder's intent with the need for accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : ما حكم تولية القاضي الناظر حسبة مع وجود الناظر المشروط له؟ قلت : صحيحة إذا شك الناظر أو ارتاب القاضي في أمانته لقول الخصاف كما نقلناه عنه، وأما إذا أدخل رجلاً الخ لا يأخذ من معلوم المتولي ولا من الوقف شيئاً لأنه إنما ولاه القاضي حسبة أي بغير معلوم
If you say: What is the ruling of the qadi appointing a nazir pro bono while there exists a nazir stipulated [by the waqf founder]? I say: It is valid if the nazir doubts or the qadi suspects his trustworthiness, according to the statement of Al-Khassaf as we transmitted from him. As for if he brings in a man, etc., he does not take from the stipend of the trustee or from the waqf anything because the qadi only appointed him pro bono, i.e., without compensation.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario: the waqf founder designated a specific nazir. If that nazir becomes untrustworthy or the qadi doubts his integrity, the qadi may appoint another nazir to oversee the waqf pro bono. The authority for this is Al-Khassaf. The qadi's appointee should not take any compensation from the waqf or the trustee's stipend, as his appointment is voluntary (hissba). This ensures the waqf is protected without burdening it financially.

Key Terms
ناظر (nazir): Supervisor of a waqf, appointed by the waqf founder or qadi.
حسبة (hissba): Service rendered voluntarily without compensation, often for public benefit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is the qadi's appointment of a pro bono nazir valid despite the existence of a nazir stipulated by the waqf founder?
A) Always
B) When the original nazir is trustworthy
C) When the qadi doubts the original nazir's trustworthiness
D) When the waqf founder permits

Key Takeaway
The qadi's authority to appoint a pro bono nazir when the stipulated nazir's trustworthiness is in doubt safeguards the waqf's integrity without overriding the founder's intent absolutely.

Self-Dismissal and Vacating the Nazir Post: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on trustee's self-dismissal and intra-Hanafi conflict on vacating the nazir post.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid self-dismissal of a waqf trustee and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on vacating the nazir post.

Core Idea
A trustee's self-dismissal requires the qadi's knowledge; vacating the nazir post is only valid in death sickness, not in health.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi conflict. The author initially suggests that a trustee may vacate his post for another, but then confronts earlier authoritative texts that forbid it during health except with the founder's permission. The resolution hinges on distinguishing between the nazir of a waqf and other post holders like teachers or imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on self-dismissal
Determine the legal effect of a trustee saying 'I dismiss myself' in the qadi's absence. The text states he is not dismissed until the qadi knows.
This is analogous to the rulings for executors (wasi) and judges.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute on vacating the nazir post
The author's initial statement permitting vacating the nazir post contradicts earlier transmissions from Al-Zuhairiyya and Al-Ashbah, which restrict such vacating to death sickness or with the waqf founder's permission.
The contradictory positions are both Hanafi; the resolution is a tarjih (preference) within the school.
3
Trace the reasoning of each side
The permissive view is supported by the fatwa of 'Allama Qasim that the qadi is not obligated to confirm the appointee. The restrictive view relies on the principle that delegation during health requires general permission from the waqf founder.
The author later distinguishes between posts, limiting permissibility to non-nazir roles.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If a nazir vacates in health, the vacating is ineffective; the qadi is not bound to confirm the appointee and the post remains under the original nazir until proper removal.
For other posts like teaching, vacating during health may be valid as per the fatwa.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (relied-upon position)
The author of Al-Bahr al-Raiq indicates the relied-upon view is that a nazir cannot vacate in health; permissibility is restricted to other posts. This is consistent with earlier Hanafi masters.
The distiction is reinforced by a later passage in Al-Ashbah regarding the nazir being a deputy (wakil) of the waqf founder.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع إذا عزل نفسه عند القاضي فإنه ينصب غيره وهل ينعزل بعزل نفسه في غيبة القاضي؟ الجواب لا ينعزل حتى يبلغ القاضي كما صرحوا به في الوصي والقاضي، وظاهر كلامهم في كتاب القضاء أنه ينعزل إذا علم القاضي سواء عزله القاضي أو لم يعزله . وفي القنية : لو قال المتولي من جهة الواقف عزلت نفسي لا ينعزل إلا أن يقول له أو للقاضي فيخرجه اهـ. ومن عزل نفسه الفراغ عن وظيفة النظر لرجل عند القاضي. وهل يجب على القاضي أن يقرر المنزول له وهكذا في سائر الوظائف، فإن لم يكن المنزول له أهلاً لا شك أنه لا يقرره، وإن كان أهلاً فكذلك لا يجب عليه وأفتى العلامة قاسم بأن من فرغ لإنسان عن لم يلزمه شيء. ولا ينعزل إلا بإذن القاضي. أقول : بقي هنا شيء وهو أن ما ذكره المؤلف من صحة الفراغ عن وظيفة النظر مخالف لما قدمه قبل ورقة ونصف نقلاً عن الظهيرية بقوله : المتولي إذا أراد أن يفوض إلى غيره عند الموت إن كان الولاية بالإيصاء يجوز وإن أراد أن يقيم غيره مقام نفسه في صحته وحياته لا يجوز إلا إذا كان التفويض إليه على سبيل التعميم .اهـ. وحاصله أن القيم ليس له أن ينزل عن وظيفة النظر إلا في مرض موته على سبيل الإيصاء، وأما في صحته فلا إلا إذا كان الواقف أذن له بذلك ومر بيانه فيما نقلناه عن الطرسوسي. وعن هذا قال في الأشباه في أواخر كتاب الإقرار ونقله عن العلائي أيضاً ما نصه الفعل في المرض أحط رتبة من الفعل في الصحة إلا في مسألة إسناد الناظر النظر لغيره بلا شرط فإنه في مرض الموت صحيح لا في الصحة كما في التتمة وغيرها اهـ. فهذا هو المنقول في مسألة الناظر فليحمل ما ذكره المؤلف هنا من جواز النزول عن الوظائف على غير وظيفة النظر كوظيفة تدريس وإمامة ونحو ذلك . وإن حمل جواز النزول عن النظر على ما إذا كان عند القاضي يحتاج إلى نقل صريح يخصص به كلامهم والمؤلف لم ينقل ذلك هنا تأمل. هذا وقد ذكر في الأشباه أوائل كتاب الوقف أن الواقف إذا شرط عزل الناظر حال الوقف صح اتفاقاً وإلا لا عند ويصح عند أبي يوسف. ثم قال : ولم أر حكم عزله للمدرس والإمام الذي ولاهما ولا يمكن الإلحاق بالناظر لتعليلهم لصحة عزله عند الثاني بكونه وكيلاً عنه وليس صاحب الوظيفة وكيلاً عن الواقف الخ. فهذا يفيد الفرق بين الناظر وغيره من أصحاب الوظائف فليتأمل. قوله: (وأفتى العلامة قاسم بأن من فرغ لإنسان الخ) قال الرملي : هذا صريح في صحة تقرير الناظر لغيره، سواء علم بفراغه لدى القاضي أم لا، لأنه عزل ولا يجب عليه تقريره، ويؤخذ منه أنه لو مات ذو وظيفة فقرر الناظر آخر فبان أنه نزل عنها لآخر لم يقدح ذلك في التقرير كما أفتى به بعض الشافعية، بل لو قرره مع علمه بذلك فكذلك كما صرح به بعضهم وقواعدنا تقتضي ذلك، ولأنه حيث كان عزلاً فقد شغرت الوظيفة لعدم تقرير القاضي فيجب التقييد بما إذا لم يقرر القاضي المنزول له لأنه لو صح
Fourth: If he dismisses himself before the qadi, then he appoints another. Is he dismissed by his self-dismissal in the qadi's absence? Answer: He is not dismissed until it reaches the qadi, as they stated regarding the executor and the judge. And the apparent meaning of their words in the book of Qada is that he is dismissed if the qadi knows, whether the qadi dismisses him or not. In Al-Qunyah: If the mutawalli appointed by the waqf founder says 'I have dismissed myself,' he is not dismissed unless he says it to him or to the qadi, so he removes him. And whoever dismisses himself is vacating the post of nazir for a person before the qadi. Is it obligatory on the qadi to confirm the one for whom the post is vacated? Similarly for all posts. If the person for whom it is vacated is not qualified, no doubt he is not confirmed. If he is qualified, likewise it is not obligatory. And 'Allama Qasim gave a fatwa that whoever vacates for a person does not become obligated by it. And he is not dismissed except by the qadi's permission. I say: There remains a point: what the author mentioned about the validity of vacating the post of nazir contradicts what he presented a sheet and a half earlier, quoting from Al-Zuhayriyyah: The mutawalli when he wants to delegate to another at the time of death, if the authority is by will, it is permissible; if he wants to appoint another in his place during his health and life, it is not permissible unless the delegation was on the basis of generality. The conclusion is that the qayyim may not step down from the post of nazir except in his death sickness by way of will. In his health, only if the waqf founder permitted it. And from this, it is stated in Al-Ashbah at the end of the book of Iqrara, and transmitted from Al-Ala'i: the action in sickness is lower in rank than action in health, except in the matter of the nazir assigning the oversight to another without condition, for it is valid in death sickness, not in health, as in Al-Tatmimah and others. So this is the transmitted position on the matter of the nazir. So what the author mentioned here about the permissibility of stepping down from posts should be applied to other than the post of nazir, like posts of teaching, imamate, and the like. And if one interprets the permissibility of stepping down from nazir as when it is before the qadi, it needs an explicit transmission to specify their words, and the author did not transmit that here. Consider. And it was mentioned in Al-Ashbah at the beginning of the book of Waqf that if the waqf founder stipulates the dismissal of the nazir at the time of waqf, it is valid unanimously, otherwise it is not valid according to some, and valid according to Abu Yusuf. Then he said: I have not seen the ruling on his dismissal of the teacher and imam whom he appointed, and it cannot be analogized to the nazir because they justify its validity according to the second (Abu Yusuf) because he is his deputy, and the holder of the post is not a deputy of the waqf founder. This shows the difference between the nazir and other post holders. So reflect. His statement: 'And 'Allama Qasim gave a fatwa...' Al-Ramli said: This is explicit about the validity of the nazir confirming someone else, whether he knows of his vacating before the qadi or not, because it is dismissal and he is not obligated to confirm him. And it is derived from it that if a post holder died and the nazir confirmed another, and it became apparent that he had stepped down for another, that does not harm the confirmation, as some Shafi'is gave fatwa. Even if he confirmed it with knowledge of that, it is the same as some stated, and our principles require that. And because where it is a dismissal, the post becomes vacant due to the lack of confirmation by the qadi, so it must be restricted to when the qadi has not confirmed the person for whom it is vacated, because if he confirmed...
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This extensive passage discusses the self-dismissal ('azl nafs) of the waqf trustee and the concept of vacating the post (firagh) for another. The main ruling: a trustee cannot dismiss himself simply by saying so; the dismissal only takes effect when the qadi knows. However, the qadi is not obligated to confirm the person designated by the trustee who vacates. The passage then highlights a contradiction: earlier, from Al-Zuhairiyya, it was stated that the trustee cannot delegate during health, only in death sickness by will. The commentator resolves this by saying the permissibility of vacating applies to non-nazir posts (like teaching), not to the nazir of a waqf. The discussion also includes the difference between the nazir and other post holders regarding dismissal. The fatwa of 'Allama Qasim and Al-Ramli's commentary further clarify that the qadi is not bound by the trustee's appointment.

Key Terms
عزل نفسه ('azl nafsihi): Self-dismissal of the trustee by his own statement, which is not effective until qadi knows.
فراغ (firagh): Vacating the post (function) for another person, akin to resignation with handover.
نزول عن الوظيفة (nuzul 'an al-wazifa): Stepping down from a post, often in exchange for compensation; debated in Hanafi waqf law.
تقرير (taqrir): Confirmation by the qadi of a person designated by the vacating trustee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a trustee's self-dismissal (عزل نفسه) in the absence of the qadi?
A) It is effective immediately
B) It is not effective until the qadi knows
C) It is effective only if a witness is present
D) It is effective only if written

Key Takeaway
Self-dismissal requires qadi's knowledge; vacating the nazir post is only valid in death sickness or with founder's permission, not in health.

The Ruling on Faraagh (Vacating a Waqf Position for Money)
A ruling statement on the permissibility of vacating a waqf position for money.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on faraagh (vacating a waqf position for money) and explain why it is discouraged.

Core Idea
Faraagh with money is a problematic practice; the narrator should seek a general acquittance.

In this brief passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the author notes the common Egyptian custom of paying to vacate a waqf position. While not explicitly prohibited, the practice is viewed with disapproval. Let's examine the ruling and its basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that faraagh refers to vacating a waqf position (like nazir) in exchange for money.
2
Note the author's reaction
The author says 'ولا يخفى ما فيه' meaning the problematic nature is not hidden.
3
Recognize the recommended action
The author recommends a general acquittance (الإبراء العام) to clear future liabilities.
4
Understand the underlying reason
The consideration (money) is for a mere right (haqq mujarrad), not a tangible asset, making the transaction doubtful.
5
Conclude the ruling
The ruling is makruh tanzihi (discouraged, not prohibited).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وظيفته سقط حقه منها سواء قرر الناظر المنزول له أو لا. اهـ. فالقاضي بالأولى، وقد جرى التعارف بمصر الفراغ بالدراهم ولا يخفى ما فيه وينبغي الإبراء العام بعده. وفي البزازية: المتولي من جهة الحاكم امتنع من العمل ولم يرفع الأمر بعزل نفسه إلى الحاكم لا يخرج عن التولية اهـ. فإن قلت: هل للقاضي عزل من ولاه بغير جنحة؟ قلت: نعم. قال في القنية: نصب القاضي قيماً آخر لا ينعزل الأول إن كان منصوب الواقف، وإن كان منصوبه ويعلمه وقت نصب الثاني ينعزل بخلاف ما إذا نصب السلطان قاضياً في بلدة لا ينعزل الأول على أحد القولين لأنه قد تكثر القضاة في بلدة دون القوام في الوقف في مسجد واحد اهـ. وسيأتي عن الخانية أنه مقيد بما إذا رأى المصلحة.
His dues drop from it [the position] whether the nazir confirms the one who is removed or not. End. So the qadi is even more entitled. And the custom in Egypt has become vacating with dirhams, and it is not hidden what is in it. It is better to have a general acquittance afterwards. In al-Bazzaziyyah: The mutawalli appointed by the ruler refrains from work and does not raise the matter for self-removal to the ruler; he does not exit the trusteeship. End. If you say: Can the qadi remove the one he appointed without misconduct? I say: Yes. He said in al-Qunyah: The qadi appoints another qayyim; the first is not removed if he was appointed by the waqif. But if he was his appointee and he knows the time of the second appointment, he is removed, unlike if the sultan appointed a qadi in a town; the first is not removed according to one of two opinions because qadis may increase in a town while custodians in a single mosque do not. End. It will come from al-Khaniyyah that it is restricted to when he sees the maslaha.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq deals with two interconnected issues: First, the practice of 'faraagh' (vacating a waqf position) in exchange for money. The text notes this is common in Egypt but implies it is problematic, advising a general acquittance. Second, it discusses whether a qadi can remove a nazir he appointed without proven misconduct. The author confirms from al-Qunyah that yes, he can, but then notes from al-Khaniyyah that this power is restricted to cases where the qadi sees maslaha (public interest). The passage also differentiates between a nazir appointed by the waqif (who cannot be removed by a later qadi) and one appointed by a qadi (who can be removed). It also compares to the sultan's appointment of qadis, where removal is disputed. The underlying Hanafi principle is that the qadi's authority over his appointed nazir is not automatic but subject to considerations of the waqf's interests.

Key Terms
فارغ (الفراغ) (faraagh): Vacating a waqf position (like nazir) in exchange for consideration, customarily done with money.
إبراء عام (ibraa' 'aam): A general acquittance, a declaration clearing the outgoing nazir from any future claims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author recommend after a faraagh with dirhams?
A) Ignore it
B) General acquittance
C) Oath
D) New contract

Key Takeaway
Faraagh (vacating a waqf position) for money is discouraged; a general acquittance should be obtained to avoid future claims.

Can a Qadi Remove His Appointed Nazir Without Misconduct?
An intra-Hanafi dispute on the qadi's authority to remove a nazir without cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on a qadi's power to remove a nazir he appointed, including the condition of maslaha and the distinction between waqif-appointed and qadi-appointed nazirs.

Core Idea
A qadi may remove his appointed nazir without misconduct only when he sees maslaha; a waqif-appointed nazir cannot be removed.

This passage delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute: can a qadi remove a nazir he appointed without proven misconduct? The author reconciles conflicting sources by imposing the condition of maslaha. Let's follow the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central question
The passage asks: هل للقاضي عزل من ولاه بغير جنحة؟ (Can the qadi remove his appointee without misconduct?)
2
Note the initial answer
The author answers: نعم (Yes).
3
Contrast with the analogy to the sultan's qadi
If the sultan appoints a qadi in a town, a second appointment does not automatically remove the first, because multiple qadis can exist in one town. But for a nazir in a mosque, multiple custodians cause confusion.
4
Understand the distinction based on appointor
If the nazir was appointed by the waqif, the qadi cannot remove him. If the nazir was appointed by the qadi himself, the qadi can remove him by appointing another.
5
Reconcile with al-Khaniyyah's condition
The power to remove is restricted to when the qadi sees maslaha (public interest), reconciling conflicting sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وظيفته سقط حقه منها سواء قرر الناظر المنزول له أو لا. اهـ. فالقاضي بالأولى، وقد جرى التعارف بمصر الفراغ بالدراهم ولا يخفى ما فيه وينبغي الإبراء العام بعده. وفي البزازية: المتولي من جهة الحاكم امتنع من العمل ولم يرفع الأمر بعزل نفسه إلى الحاكم لا يخرج عن التولية اهـ. فإن قلت: هل للقاضي عزل من ولاه بغير جنحة؟ قلت: نعم. قال في القنية: نصب القاضي قيماً آخر لا ينعزل الأول إن كان منصوب الواقف، وإن كان منصوبه ويعلمه وقت نصب الثاني ينعزل بخلاف ما إذا نصب السلطان قاضياً في بلدة لا ينعزل الأول على أحد القولين لأنه قد تكثر القضاة في بلدة دون القوام في الوقف في مسجد واحد اهـ. وسيأتي عن الخانية أنه مقيد بما إذا رأى المصلحة.
His dues drop from it [the position] whether the nazir confirms the one who is removed or not. End. So the qadi is even more entitled. And the custom in Egypt has become vacating with dirhams, and it is not hidden what is in it. It is better to have a general acquittance afterwards. In al-Bazzaziyyah: The mutawalli appointed by the ruler refrains from work and does not raise the matter for self-removal to the ruler; he does not exit the trusteeship. End. If you say: Can the qadi remove the one he appointed without misconduct? I say: Yes. He said in al-Qunyah: The qadi appoints another qayyim; the first is not removed if he was appointed by the waqif. But if he was his appointee and he knows the time of the second appointment, he is removed, unlike if the sultan appointed a qadi in a town; the first is not removed according to one of two opinions because qadis may increase in a town while custodians in a single mosque do not. End. It will come from al-Khaniyyah that it is restricted to when he sees the maslaha.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq deals with two interconnected issues: First, the practice of 'faraagh' (vacating a waqf position) in exchange for money. The text notes this is common in Egypt but implies it is problematic, advising a general acquittance. Second, it discusses whether a qadi can remove a nazir he appointed without proven misconduct. The author confirms from al-Qunyah that yes, he can, but then notes from al-Khaniyyah that this power is restricted to cases where the qadi sees maslaha (public interest). The passage also differentiates between a nazir appointed by the waqif (who cannot be removed by a later qadi) and one appointed by a qadi (who can be removed). It also compares to the sultan's appointment of qadis, where removal is disputed. The underlying Hanafi principle is that the qadi's authority over his appointed nazir is not automatic but subject to considerations of the waqf's interests.

Key Terms
ناظر (nazir): The administrator of a waqf, appointed either by the waqif or by a qadi.
عزل بغير جنحة (azl bi-ghayr janhah): Removal from a waqf position by the appointing authority without proven misconduct.
مصلحة (maslaha): Public interest or benefit, used as a condition for the qadi's removal power.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Khaniyyah, when can a qadi remove a nazir he appointed?
A) Any time
B) Only with khayanah
C) When he sees maslaha
D) When the nazir agrees

Key Takeaway
A qadi may remove his appointed nazir without misconduct provided he perceives maslaha; a waqif-appointed nazir is immune from removal.

Nazir's Duties and Leasing Rules: The Khayar Exception
Ruling on nazir's duties and self-leasing with qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nazir's primary duty in managing waqf income and apply the rule for leasing waqf property to himself or relatives, including the khayar condition.

Core Idea
The nazir must prioritize repairs, and may lease to self only with a khayar for beneficiaries — avoiding tuhma.

Waqf administration requires meticulous care to avoid conflicts of interest. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq outlines the nazir's first financial obligation — repairs and wages — and then addresses the sensitive issue of self-dealing: leasing waqf property to oneself or relatives. The key is the 'khayar' (beneficial option), which transforms a suspicious transaction into a permissible one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nazir's primary duty
The passage begins by stating the first thing a qayyim (nazir) must do with waqf income: initiate repairs (عمارة) and pay custodians' wages (أجرة القوام), even if the waqif did not stipulate this. Recognize this as a binding priority.
This duty is wajib, and does not require explicit instruction from the founder.
2
State the general rule on self-leasing
The text says leasing the waqf to oneself (أجر الوقف من نفسه) or residing in it for fair rent is not permissible. Similarly, leasing to close relatives (son, father, slave, mukatab) is prohibited due to tuhma (suspicion of bias).
Tuhma is the operative cause (illa) for prohibition.
3
Follow the qiyas from the guardian's sale
The passage draws an analogy: a guardian selling his own property to an orphan is valid only if it includes a beneficial option (khayar) for the orphan. This same reasoning applies to the nazir's leasing.
This is qiyas jaliy: the illa is the potential self-dealing, and the khayar protects the beneficiary.
4
Understand the khayar exception
According to Abu Hanifa, if the nazir leases to himself or his relative with a khayar for the waqf's beneficiaries, the lease becomes valid. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) reject this exception.
The fatwa (mufta bihi) is on Abu Hanifa's view, as stated: 'وبه يفتي'.
5
Analyze the ruling for relatives
For relatives, Abu Hanifa additionally requires the rent to exceed the fair rent (أكثر من أجر المثل) unless a khayar is provided. The Sahibayn are stricter.
The text says: 'لم يجز عند أبي حنيفة إلا بأكثر من أجر المثل' (not valid unless with more than fair rent) and then mentions the khayar alternative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الموضع الرابع في تصرفات الناظر وفيه بيان ما عليه وله من المعلوم أول ما يفعله القيم في غلة الوقف البداءة بالعمارة وأجرة القوام وإن لم يشترطها الواقف، ويتحرى في تصرفاته النظر للوقف والغبطة حتى لو آجر الوقف من نفسه أو سكنه بأجرة المثل لا يجوز، وكذا إذا أجره من ابنه أو أبيه أو عبده أو مكاتبه للتهمة ولا نظر معها؛ كذا في الإسعاف. وفي جامع الفصولين: المتولي لو آجر دار الوقف من ابنه البالغ أو أبيه لم يجز عند أبي حنيفة إلا بأكثر من أجر المثل كبيع الوصي لو بقيمته صح عن عندهما، ولو خيراً لليتيم صح عند أبي حنيفة، وكذا متول أجر من نفسه لو خيراً صح وإلا لا، ومعنى الخيرية مر في بيع الوصي من نفسه وبه يفتي اهـ.
The fourth topic: On the nazir's transactions. It contains an explanation of what is upon him and what he receives of the known salary. The first thing the qayyim should do with the waqf's produce is to begin with repairs and the wages of the custodians, even if the waqif did not stipulate it. He should act cautiously in his transactions, looking out for the waqf's interest and benefit. So much so that if he leases the waqf to himself or resides in it for the fair rent, it is not permissible. Similarly, if he leases it to his son, father, slave, or mukatab, due to suspicion, and there is no consideration along with it. Thus in al-Is'af. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: The mutawalli, if he leases a waqf house to his adult son or father, it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa unless with more than the fair rent, like the sale by a guardian of his own property to [the orphan] is valid? According to both [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. And if with a beneficial option (khayar) for the orphan, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa. Similarly, if a mutawalli leases to himself with a beneficial option, it is valid; otherwise no. The meaning of khayar has been mentioned in the sale of a guardian to himself, and with it fatwa is given. End.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage lays out the basic principles governing a waqf nazir's (administrator's) actions. It begins by stating his primary duties: the first priority in using waqf income is repairs and paying custodians' wages, even if not stipulated by the waqif. Then it discusses leasing. The core rule is that the nazir cannot lease waqf property to himself or to close relatives (son, father, slave, mukatab) because of tuhma (suspicion of self-dealing). However, there is a way around it: if the lease is made with a 'khayar' (beneficial option) for the waqf's beneficiaries (e.g., the orphan), it becomes valid according to Abu Hanifa. The text analogizes this to a guardian selling his own goods to an orphan—permissible if there is a khayar. The ruling differs between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): Abu Hanifa allows the khayar exception; the Sahibayn restrict it further. The fatwa is given with Abu Hanifa's view.

Key Terms
تصرفات الناظر (tasarrufat al-nazir): The transactions and decisions made by the waqf administrator (nazir)
خير (khayar): A beneficial option (option to rescind) granted to the waqf's beneficiaries to protect against disadvantage.
تهمة (tuhma): Suspicion of personal interest or bias that invalidates a fiduciary's transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when is it permissible for a nazir to lease waqf property to himself?
A) When the rent is above market rate.
B) When there is a beneficial khayar for the waqf beneficiaries.
C) When the qadi approves.
D) It is never permissible.

Key Takeaway
A nazir may not lease waqf property to himself or relatives unless a beneficial option (khayar) is granted to the beneficiaries, per Abu Hanifa's view which is the basis for fatwa.

Handling Increased Rent on Waqf Property
procedural ruling on waqf rent increase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure when the rental value of waqf property increases and apply it to different scenarios of occupant status and nature of the increase.

Core Idea
The valid lessee has a right of first refusal but must meet a genuine market increase; vexatious offers are rejected.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the Hanafi procedure when the rental value of a waqf property rises during a lease. The ruling protects both the waqf's interests and the lessee's rights, ensuring fairness. It distinguishes between valid and invalid lessees, and between genuine and vexatious increases, and also addresses agricultural land issues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the occupant's status
Determine if the current occupant is a valid lessee (sahih al-ijarah), an invalid lessee (fasid al-ijarah), or not a lessee at all. This determines whether they have any right at all.
A valid lessee has rights; others have none.
2
Classify the nature of the increase
If the occupant is a valid lessee, check if the increase is vexatious (ta'annut, from a few individuals without market basis) or genuine (by al-kull, reflecting fair market value). Only genuine increases trigger the procedure.
Vexatious increases are not accepted at all.
3
Apply the right of first refusal
For a genuine increase, the mutawalli must present the new rent to the valid lessee. If the lessee accepts, he stays and pays the new rent; if he refuses, the property is leased to the second party.
The lessee cannot block the increase by merely refusing.
4
Consider agricultural land specifics
If the property is cultivated land with a justified crop (e.g., sown by the valid lessee), the lease cannot be transferred mid-season. The increase is due from the current lessee from the time of increase, and past years' rent is accounted accordingly.
An unjustified crop (e.g., usurper's) does not prevent transfer.
5
Examine fatwa applications
Review the two fatwa cases: (1) lessee subleasing at a loss is valid because his usufruct rights become his private property; (2) after subleasing, increased offers should be presented to the first lessee (the original lessee).
These illustrate the principles in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحاصل كلامهم في الزيادة أن الساكن لو كان غير مستأجر أو مستأجراً إجارة فاسدة فإنه لا حق له وتقبل الزيادة ويخرج ويسلم المتولي العين إلى المستأجر، وإن كان مستأجراً صحيحة، فإن كانت تعنتاً فهي غير مقبولة أصلاً، وإن كانت لزيادة أجر المثل عند الكل عرض المتولي الزيادة على المستأجر، فإن قبلها فهو الأحق وإلا آجرها من الثاني فإن كانت أرضاً فهي كغيرها لكن إن كانت الأرض خالية عن الزراعة أجرها للثاني وإلا وجبت الزيادة على المستأجر الأول من وقتها ووجب تسليم السنين الماضية والمسمى بحسابه قبلها لأن الزرع مانع من صحة الإجارة حيث كان مزروعاً بحق وهذا كذلك. وإن لم يكن مزروعاً بحق كالغاصب والمستأجر إجارة فاسدة فإنه لا يمنع صحة الإجارة كما في الظهيرية والسراجية لكونه لا يمنع التسليم، فإن كان المتولي مع قدرته على الرفع لا غرامة عليه وقد وقعت حوادث الفتوى منها: استأجر أرض الوقف بأجر المثل ثم أجرها لآخر بأقل بنقصان فاحش فأجبت بالصحة لأن المنافع المملوكة للمستأجر ليست كالوقف وإنما هي كالملك ولذا ملك الإعارة ومنها لو زاد أجر المثل بعد ما أجر المستأجر هل يعرض الأمر على الأول أم الثاني؟ فأجبت على الأول لأنه المستأجر من هذه.
The upshot of their statements concerning the increase is that the occupant, if he is not a lessee or is a lessee under a void lease, then he has no right and the increase is accepted, and he vacates and the mutawalli delivers the asset to the lessee. But if he is a valid lessee, then if the increase is vexatious, it is not accepted at all. If it is for an increase in the fair rent by all, the mutawalli presents the increase to the lessee. If he accepts it, then he is more entitled; otherwise, he leases it to the second. If it is land, it is like other property, but if the land is free of cultivation, he leases to the second; otherwise, the increase is obligatory on the first lessee from its time, and delivery of past years and the named rent by its account before it is obligatory because the crop prevents the validity of the lease if it was sown justifiably, and this is so. If it was not sown justifiably, like a usurper or a lessee under a void lease, then it does not prevent the validity of the lease, as in al-Zahirah and al-Sirajiyyah, because it does not prevent delivery. If the mutawalli was able to remove it, there is no guarantee on him. Indeed, fatwa incidents have occurred. Among them: one leased waqf land at fair rent, then leased it to another at less with a gross deficiency. I answered with validity because the benefits owned by the lessee are not like the waqf; they are like property, and thus he owns lending. Among them: if the fair rent increased after the lessee had leased, is the matter presented to the first or the second? I answered: to the first, because he is the lessee from this.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the procedure when the rental value of waqf property increases during the lease term. The key distinction is whether the current occupant is a valid lessee or not. If the occupant is not a valid lessee (e.g., a squatter or someone with a void lease), they have no right and the mutawalli can accept a higher offer from a new tenant. If the occupant is a valid lessee, the mutawalli must first offer the increased rent to him. If the increase is merely vexatious (a small number offering out of spite), it is not accepted. But if the increase reflects a genuine market rise, the current lessee gets priority if he matches the new rent. For agricultural land, the presence of a justified crop affects the timing: if the land is sown rightfully, the increased rent is due from the current lessee from the time of increase, but the lease cannot be transferred mid-crop. The text also cites fatwa cases: e.g., a lessee subleasing at a loss is valid because his benefits are his private property; and regarding presenting increased offers to the first lessee. The underlying Hanafi principle prioritizes the existing lessee's right but prevents him from blocking legitimate market adjustments.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyada): An increase in the rental value of waqf property after a lease is in effect.
تعنت (ta'annut): Vexatious or spiteful increase offered by one or two individuals without genuine market cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a valid lessee refuses to accept a genuine increase in rent, what happens?
A) He is forced to pay the increase.
B) The mutawalli leases to the second party.
C) The increase is void.
D) The lessee retains his right.

Key Takeaway
The valid lessee's right of first refusal protects his stability but cannot block genuine market increases for the waqf.

Condition for a Valid Increase and Priority of the Current Lessee
Initial ruling on condition of increase and classification of occupant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a valid rent increase on waqf property and explain the procedure for presenting the increase to the current lessee.

Core Idea
A spiteful bid by one or two individuals does not create a valid increase; only a general market rise triggers the offer to the current lessee.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq lays out the foundational rule for increases in rent on waqf property. The mutawalli must differentiate between a genuine market increase and a malicious bid. A valid lessee has the right of first refusal; others do not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for a valid increase
The increase must be from the general public (ʿinda al-kull), not from one or two spiteful individuals. Read the first line: 'Wa sharṭ al-ziyādah an takūn ʿinda al-kull.'
This protects the current lessee from vindictive bids.
2
Classify the occupant
Determine if the occupant is a valid lessee, a defective lessee, or not a lessee. Only a valid lessee has the right to match the increase.
A defective lease (fāsid) means the occupant has no prior right.
3
Apply the procedure for a valid lessee
If the increase is genuine (due to market rise), the mutawalli presents it to the current lessee. If the lessee accepts, he stays; if not, the mutawalli leases to the second bidder.
The lessee's acceptance must cover the new rent.
4
Reject spiteful increases outright
If the increase is from one or two out of spite, it is not accepted at all, and the current lessee continues at the original rent.
This prevents harm to the lessee from malicious bidders.

الزيادة ويخرج ويسلم المتولي العين إلى المستأجر، وإن كان مستأجراً صحيحة، فإن كانت تعنتاً فهي غير مقبولة أصلاً، وإن كانت لزيادة أجر المثل عند الكل عرض المتولي الزيادة على المستأجر، فإن قبلها فهو الأحق وإلا آجرها من الثاني فإن كانت أرضاً فهي كغيرها لكن إن كانت الأرض خالية عن الزراعة أجرها للثاني وإلا وجبت الزيادة على المستأجر الأول من وقتها ووجب تسليم السنين الماضية والمسمى بحسابه قبلها لأن الزرع مانع من صحة الإجارة حيث كان مزروعاً بحق وهذا كذلك. وإن لم يكن مزروعاً بحق كالغاصب والمستأجر إجارة فاسدة فإنه لا يمنع صحة الإجارة كما في الظهيرية والسراجية لكونه لا يمنع التسليم، فإن كان المتولي مع قدرته على الرفع لا غرامة عليه وقد وقعت حوادث الفتوى منها : استأجر أرض الوقف بأجر المثل ثم أجرها لآخر بأقل بنقصان فاحش فأجبت بالصحة لأن المنافع المملوكة للمستأجر ليست كالوقف وإنما هي كالملك ولذا ملك الإعارة ومنها لو زاد أجر المثل بعد ما أجر المستأجر هل يعرض الأمر على الأول أم الثاني ؟ فأجبت على الأول لأنه المستأجر من المتولي. ومنها لو لم يقبل ونقضت وأجرها المتولي ممن زاد هل تنتقض الثانية؟ فأجبت تنتقض لكونها مبنية على الأولى فإذا انتقض الأصل انتقض ما ابتنى عليه كما في الفتاوى الصغرى من الإجارة الطويلة، وعلى هذا لو فسخت الأولى بخيار رؤية أو عيب بقضاء بطلت الثانية . ومنها لو أجر المتولي جميع جهات الوقف الخراجي والهلالي بأجرة المثل فزاد أجر مثل بعضها وزاد فيها غيره هل تؤجر من الآخر بعد العرض على الأول أو لا؟ فأجبت ينبغي أن لا تقبل الزيادة لأنه حيث استأجر الجميع إجارة واحدة إنما ينظر إلى زيادة أجرة الجميع لا كل واحدة. ومنها أنه كيف يعلم القاضي أن الزيادة بسبب زيادة أجر المثل؟ وهل يحتاج إلى إثبات ذلك؟ قلت : نعم لما في الخانية من كتاب الوصايا وصي باع شيئاً من مال اليتيم ثم طلب منه بأكثر مما باع فإن القاضي يرجع إلى أهل البصر؛ إن أخبره اثنان من أهل البصر والأمانة أنه باع بقيمته وإن قيمته ذلك فإن القاضي لا يلتفت إلى من يريد، وإن كان في المزايدة يشتري بأكثر وفي السوق بأقل لا ينتقض بيع الوصي لأجل تلك الزيادة بل يرجع إلى أهل البصر والأمانة، وإن اجتمع رجلان منهم على شيء يؤخذ بقولهما معاً، وهذا قول محمد، أما على قولهما قول الواحد يكفي كما في التزكية ونحوها وعلى هذا قيم الوقف إذا أجر مستغل الوقف وجاء آخر يزيد في الأجرة .اهـ. وصرح قاضيخان من كتاب الإجارة بأنه إذا أجر بأقل من أجرة المثل ؛ فإن كان بنقصان يتغابن الناس فيه فهي صحيحة وليس للمتولي فسخها، وإن كان بنقصان لا يتغابن الناس فيه فهي فاسدة وله أن يؤاجرها إجارة صحيحة إما من الأول أو من غيره بأجر المثل وبالزيادة على قدر ما يرضى به المستأجر، فإن سكن المستأجر الأول وجب أجر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ وعليه الفتوى وإن كانت الإجارة الأولى بأجرة المثل ثم ازداد أجر مثله كان للمتولي أن يفسخ الإجارة، وما لم يفسخ كان على المستأجر الأجر المسمى اهـ. وفي الحاوي: ويفتي بالضمان في غصب عقار الوقف وغصب منافعه، وكذا كل ما بيده إلى انتهاء مدته، أما إذا فرغت مدته فما وجه كونه أحق بالإيجار من غيره؟ نعم قد يكون أحق بعلة أخرى وهي أنه لو كان المأجور أرضاً له عليها بناء أو غراس أو نحو ذلك وكان يرضى بدفع أجرة المثل لتلك الأرض خالية عن البناء والغراس وهي مسألة الأرض المحتكرة لأن في إبقائها بيده دفع الضرر عنه مع عدم ضرر الوقف على أن في هذه الصورة كلاماً فإن مقتضى إطلاق المتون في كتاب الإجارة يدل على أنه لاحق له فإنه سيأتي في المتن هناك قوله : وصح للبناء والغراس فإن مضت المدة قلعهما وسلمها فارغة إلا أن يغرم له المؤجر قيمته مقلوعاً ويتملكه أو يرضى بتركه فيكون البناء والغراس لهذا والأرض لهذا .اهـ. وقد أفتى بذلك الخير الرملي وتارة أفتى بالأول نظراً للمستأجر لما فيه من رفع الضرر عنه قوله : (وإن كان الإجارة الأولى بأجرة المثل ثم ازداد أجر مثله الخ) أقول في التجنيس والمزيد لصاحب الهداية رجل استأجر أرض وقف ثلاث سنين بأجرة معلومة .
And the condition of the increase is that it be from everyone. However, if one or two persons increase it out of spite, it is not accepted, as stated by al-Asbījābī. The summary of their statements regarding the increase is that if the occupant is not a lessee or is a lessee under a defective lease, then he has no right, and the increase is accepted, and he vacates, and the mutawalli hands over the property to the lessee. And if he is a valid lessee, then if it is out of spite, it is not accepted at all. And if it is due to an increase in the market rent from everyone, the mutawalli presents the increase to the lessee; if he accepts it, then he has more right, otherwise he leases it to the second. If it is land, it is like other properties, except that if the land is free of cultivation, he leases it to the second; otherwise, the increase is due from the first lessee from the time it occurred, and the delivery of past years and the named rent according to its calculation before it is obligatory, because crops prevent the validity of the lease when they are planted by right, and this is similar. If it is not planted by right, like a usurper or a lessee under a defective lease, then it does not prevent the validity of the lease, as in al-Ẓahīriyya and al-Sirājiyya, because it does not prevent delivery. If the mutawalli is able to remove it, there is no liability on him. Fatwa incidents have occurred, among them: A person leased waqf land at market rent, then leased it to another at a lower rent with a glaring deficiency. I answered that it is valid because the benefits owned by the lessee are not like the endowment; rather they are like ownership, hence he has the right to give it as a loan. And among them: If the market rent increased after the lessee had leased it, should the matter be presented to the first or the second? I answered: to the first, because he is the lessee from the mutawalli. And among them: If he did not accept and it was rescinded, and the mutawalli leased it to the one who increased, should the second lease be rescinded? I answered: it is rescinded because it is built upon the first; if the origin is rescinded, what is built upon it is rescinded, as in al-Fatāwā al-Ṣughrā regarding long leases. And similarly, if the first lease is rescinded due to option of sighting or defect by court ruling, the second is void. And among them: If the mutawalli leased all parts of the kharājī and hilālī endowment lands at market rent, and then the market rent of some parts increased, and someone else increased for them, should it be leased to the other after presenting to the first or not? I answered: it is appropriate that the increase not be accepted, because since he leased all in one lease, only the increase of the total rent is considered, not each part. And among them: How does the judge know that the increase is due to an increase in market rent? Does it need proof? I said: Yes, because in al-Khāniyya from the book of bequests: if a guardian sold something from the orphan's property, then someone sought it from him at a higher price, the judge refers to experts; if two experts of sight and trust inform him that he sold it at its value and that its value is that, the judge does not pay attention to the one who wants more, even if there is a bidder at a higher price and in the market it is lower. The sale of the guardian is not rescinded due to that increase; rather, reference is made to experts of sight and trust. If two of them agree on something, both statements are taken together. This is the saying of Muḥammad. As for their saying (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad?), the statement of one is sufficient, as in matters of tazkiya and the like. Based on this, the same applies if the mutawalli of the endowment leases the income-generating endowment and another comes to increase the rent, etc. And Qāḍīkhān explicitly stated in the book of leases that if he leases at less than market rent, then if it is a deficiency in which people engage in mutual toleration (taghābun), it is valid and the mutawalli does not have the right to rescind it. And if it is a deficiency in which people do not engage in mutual toleration, it is legally defective (fāsid) and he may lease it validly, either from the first or from another, at market rent and at an increase to the extent that the lessee agrees. If the first lessee occupies, the market rent is due, no matter how high, and the fatwa is upon this. And if the first lease was at market rent, then its market rent increased, the mutawalli may rescind the lease, and as long as he does not rescind, the named rent is incumbent on the lessee. And in al-Ḥāwī: It is fatwa that liability (ḍamān) applies in usurpation of waqf real estate and usurpation of its usufructs, and similarly everything in his possession until the end of its term. As for when the term expires, what is the basis for his having more right to lease than others? Yes, he may have more right by another cause, namely if the leased land has a building or trees on it or the like, and he agrees to pay market rent for the land empty of the building and trees. This is the issue of the leased land (al-arḍ al-muḥtakara), because keeping it in his possession prevents harm to him without harm to the endowment. However, there is discussion about this scenario, because the absolute wording of the matn in the book of leases indicates that he has no right, for it will come in the matn there: “It is valid for the building and trees: if the term expires, he removes them and delivers the land empty, unless the lessor compensates him for their value in a removed state and takes ownership, or he agrees to leave them, in which case the building and trees are for one party and the land for the other.” And al-Khayr al-Ramlī gave fatwa according to that, and sometimes he gave fatwa according to the first view out of consideration for the lessee due to preventing harm from him. His saying: (And if the first lease was at market rent, then its market rent increased, etc.) I say in al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd of the author of al-Hidāya: A man leased waqf land for three years with a known rent.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqā'iq, discusses the rulings concerning increases in rent for waqf (endowment) properties. The passage type is a collection of rulings (ruling_statement) with expansions and fatwa incidents. The author begins by stating the condition for the increase to be accepted: it must be a general increase from the community (ʿinda al-kull). If only one or two persons increase out of spite (taʿannutan), it is not accepted. Then the author summarizes the classification of the occupant: (1) if the occupant is not a lessee or is a lessee under a defective (fāsid) lease, he has no right and the increase is accepted, and the mutawalli hands the property to the new lessee; (2) if the occupant is a valid lessee, the increase is presented to him; if he accepts it, he has priority (huwa al-aḥaqq); otherwise, the mutawalli may lease to the second. Special rules apply for land with crops: if the land has crops planted by right (bi-ḥaqq), the increase is due from the first lessee from the time it occurred, and the delivery of past years and the named rent are due because the crop prevents a valid lease to another. If the crop is not by right (e.g., usurper or defective lease), it does not prevent validity. Then the author relates several fatwa incidents: (a) A lessee at market rent who subleases at a lower rent with glaring deficiency – the sublease is valid because the lessee owns the usufructs. (b) When market rent increases after the first lease, the increase is presented to the first lessee, not the second. (c) If the first lessee does not accept and the lease is rescinded, the second lease built on it is also rescinded. (d) If the mutawalli leases all parts together, an increase on some parts is not accepted because the consideration is the total rent. (e) Proof of increase due to market rent requires expert testimony. The passage then cites Qāḍīkhān's distinction between a deficiency that people tolerate (taghābun) – in which case the lease is valid and cannot be rescinded – and one they do not tolerate, in which case the lease is defective and the mutawalli can lease at market rent. If the first lease was at market rent and then market rent increases, the mutawalli may rescind. As long as he does not rescind, the named rent is due. Finally, a discussion about the priority of the first lessee after the term expires: he is not automatically entitled, except perhaps in cases where he has buildings or trees on the land and is willing to pay market rent, but there is disagreement, with some authorities giving him priority to prevent harm. The passage emphasizes that the Hanafi position relies on the principle that benefits owned by the lessee are like ownership, and that the mutawalli acts to protect the waqf.

Key Terms
الزيادة (al-ziyādah): An increase in the rent offered for leasing waqf property, either due to market changes or a competing bid.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The fair market rent for the property at the time of lease.
متولي (mutawallī): The administrator or custodian of the waqf property, responsible for leasing it and collecting rent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in the passage, what is the condition for an increase in rent to be accepted when leasing waqf property?
A) Any increase from any person is accepted to benefit the waqf.
B) The increase must be from the general public (ʿinda al-kull), not from one or two individuals out of spite.
C) The increase must be approved by the judge.
D) The increase must be at least double the original rent.

Key Takeaway
A rent increase on waqf property is valid only if it reflects a general market rise; if it is a spiteful bid by one or two individuals, it is rejected outright.

Land with Crops and Fatwa Incidents on Waqf Leasing
Rulings on land with crops and fatwa incidents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling for land with crops planted by right and analyze fatwa incidents on subleasing and rescission of leases.

Core Idea
Crops planted by right prevent a new lease on the land, but if the lessee subleases at a loss, the sublease is valid.

This continuation of the passage addresses special considerations for agricultural waqf land and presents several fatwa incidents that illustrate the application of the general rules. The author answers questions about subleasing at a loss, rescission of second leases, and the effect of leasing all parts together.

Guided Path
1
Understand the rule for land with crops planted by right
If the land has crops planted by a valid lessee (bi-ḥaqq), the crop prevents a new lease to another. The increase is due from the first lessee from the time it occurs, and past named rent is still due.
If the crop is not by right (e.g., usurper), it does not prevent a new lease.
2
Analyze the first fatwa incident: subleasing at a loss
A lessee who rents at market rent may sublease at a lower rent with glaring deficiency. The sublease is valid because the lessee owns the benefits.
This is based on the principle that the lessee's usufruct is akin to ownership.
3
Analyze the second incident: presenting increase to the first lessee
When market rent increases, the increase must be presented to the first lessee, not the second, because the first is the lessee from the mutawalli.
This reinforces the priority of the original lessee.
4
Analyze the third incident: rescission of second lease
If the first lease is rescinded (e.g., because the lessee does not accept the increase), the second lease built on it is also rescinded.
The second lease is dependent on the first.
5
Analyze the fourth incident: increase on parts vs. whole
If the mutawalli leased all parts together in one contract, an increase on some parts is not considered; only the total increase matters.
This prevents fragmentation of a single lease.

جهات الوقف الخراجي والهلالي بأجرة المثل فزاد أجر مثل بعضها وزاد فيها غيره هل تؤجر من الآخر بعد العرض على الأول أو لا؟ فأجبت ينبغي أن لا تقبل الزيادة لأنه حيث استأجر الجميع إجارة واحدة إنما ينظر إلى زيادة أجرة الجميع لا كل واحدة. ومنها أنه كيف يعلم القاضي أن الزيادة بسبب زيادة أجر المثل؟ وهل يحتاج إلى إثبات ذلك؟ قلت : نعم لما في الخانية من كتاب الوصايا وصي باع شيئاً من مال اليتيم ثم طلب منه بأكثر مما باع فإن القاضي يرجع إلى أهل البصر؛ إن أخبره اثنان من أهل البصر والأمانة أنه باع بقيمته وإن قيمته ذلك فإن القاضي لا يلتفت إلى من يريد، وإن كان في المزايدة يشتري بأكثر وفي السوق بأقل لا ينتقض بيع الوصي لأجل تلك الزيادة بل يرجع إلى أهل البصر والأمانة، وإن اجتمع رجلان منهم على شيء يؤخذ بقولهما معاً، وهذا قول محمد، أما على قولهما قول الواحد يكفي كما في التزكية ونحوها وعلى هذا قيم الوقف إذا أجر مستغل الوقف وجاء آخر يزيد في الأجرة .اهـ. وصرح قاضيخان من كتاب الإجارة بأنه إذا أجر بأقل من أجرة المثل ؛ فإن كان بنقصان يتغابن الناس فيه فهي صحيحة وليس للمتولي فسخها، وإن كان بنقصان لا يتغابن الناس فيه فهي فاسدة وله أن يؤاجرها إجارة صحيحة إما من الأول أو من غيره بأجر المثل وبالزيادة على قدر ما يرضى به المستأجر، فإن سكن المستأجر الأول وجب أجر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ وعليه الفتوى وإن كانت الإجارة الأولى بأجرة المثل ثم ازداد أجر مثله كان للمتولي أن يفسخ الإجارة، وما لم يفسخ كان على المستأجر الأجر المسمى اهـ. وفي الحاوي: ويفتي بالضمان في غصب عقار الوقف وغصب منافعه، وكذا كل ما بيده إلى انتهاء مدته، أما إذا فرغت مدته فما وجه كونه أحق بالإيجار من غيره؟ نعم قد يكون أحق بعلة أخرى وهي أنه لو كان المأجور أرضاً له عليها بناء أو غراس أو نحو ذلك وكان يرضى بدفع أجرة المثل لتلك الأرض خالية عن البناء والغراس وهي مسألة الأرض المحتكرة لأن في إبقائها بيده دفع الضرر عنه مع عدم ضرر الوقف على أن في هذه الصورة كلاماً فإن مقتضى إطلاق المتون في كتاب الإجارة يدل على أنه لاحق له فإنه سيأتي في المتن هناك قوله : وصح للبناء والغراس فإن مضت المدة قلعهما وسلمها فارغة إلا أن يغرم له المؤجر قيمته مقلوعاً ويتملكه أو يرضى بتركه فيكون البناء والغراس لهذا والأرض لهذا .اهـ. وقد أفتى بذلك الخير الرملي وتارة أفتى بالأول نظراً للمستأجر لما فيه من رفع الضرر عنه قوله : (وإن كان الإجارة الأولى بأجرة المثل ثم ازداد أجر مثله الخ) أقول في التجنيس والمزيد لصاحب الهداية رجل استأجر أرض وقف ثلاث سنين بأجرة معلومة .
And the condition of the increase is that it be from everyone. However, if one or two persons increase it out of spite, it is not accepted, as stated by al-Asbījābī. The summary of their statements regarding the increase is that if the occupant is not a lessee or is a lessee under a defective lease, then he has no right, and the increase is accepted, and he vacates, and the mutawalli hands over the property to the lessee. And if he is a valid lessee, then if it is out of spite, it is not accepted at all. And if it is due to an increase in the market rent from everyone, the mutawalli presents the increase to the lessee; if he accepts it, then he has more right, otherwise he leases it to the second. If it is land, it is like other properties, except that if the land is free of cultivation, he leases it to the second; otherwise, the increase is due from the first lessee from the time it occurred, and the delivery of past years and the named rent according to its calculation before it is obligatory, because crops prevent the validity of the lease when they are planted by right, and this is similar. If it is not planted by right, like a usurper or a lessee under a defective lease, then it does not prevent the validity of the lease, as in al-Ẓahīriyya and al-Sirājiyya, because it does not prevent delivery. If the mutawalli is able to remove it, there is no liability on him. Fatwa incidents have occurred, among them: A person leased waqf land at market rent, then leased it to another at a lower rent with a glaring deficiency. I answered that it is valid because the benefits owned by the lessee are not like the endowment; rather they are like ownership, hence he has the right to give it as a loan. And among them: If the market rent increased after the lessee had leased it, should the matter be presented to the first or the second? I answered: to the first, because he is the lessee from the mutawalli. And among them: If he did not accept and it was rescinded, and the mutawalli leased it to the one who increased, should the second lease be rescinded? I answered: it is rescinded because it is built upon the first; if the origin is rescinded, what is built upon it is rescinded, as in al-Fatāwā al-Ṣughrā regarding long leases. And similarly, if the first lease is rescinded due to option of sighting or defect by court ruling, the second is void. And among them: If the mutawalli leased all parts of the kharājī and hilālī endowment lands at market rent, and then the market rent of some parts increased, and someone else increased for them, should it be leased to the other after presenting to the first or not? I answered: it is appropriate that the increase not be accepted, because since he leased all in one lease, only the increase of the total rent is considered, not each part. And among them: How does the judge know that the increase is due to an increase in market rent? Does it need proof? I said: Yes, because in al-Khāniyya from the book of bequests: if a guardian sold something from the orphan's property, then someone sought it from him at a higher price, the judge refers to experts; if two experts of sight and trust inform him that he sold it at its value and that its value is that, the judge does not pay attention to the one who wants more, even if there is a bidder at a higher price and in the market it is lower. The sale of the guardian is not rescinded due to that increase; rather, reference is made to experts of sight and trust. If two of them agree on something, both statements are taken together. This is the saying of Muḥammad. As for their saying (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad?), the statement of one is sufficient, as in matters of tazkiya and the like. Based on this, the same applies if the mutawalli of the endowment leases the income-generating endowment and another comes to increase the rent, etc. And Qāḍīkhān explicitly stated in the book of leases that if he leases at less than market rent, then if it is a deficiency in which people engage in mutual toleration (taghābun), it is valid and the mutawalli does not have the right to rescind it. And if it is a deficiency in which people do not engage in mutual toleration, it is legally defective (fāsid) and he may lease it validly, either from the first or from another, at market rent and at an increase to the extent that the lessee agrees. If the first lessee occupies, the market rent is due, no matter how high, and the fatwa is upon this. And if the first lease was at market rent, then its market rent increased, the mutawalli may rescind the lease, and as long as he does not rescind, the named rent is incumbent on the lessee. And in al-Ḥāwī: It is fatwa that liability (ḍamān) applies in usurpation of waqf real estate and usurpation of its usufructs, and similarly everything in his possession until the end of its term. As for when the term expires, what is the basis for his having more right to lease than others? Yes, he may have more right by another cause, namely if the leased land has a building or trees on it or the like, and he agrees to pay market rent for the land empty of the building and trees. This is the issue of the leased land (al-arḍ al-muḥtakara), because keeping it in his possession prevents harm to him without harm to the endowment. However, there is discussion about this scenario, because the absolute wording of the matn in the book of leases indicates that he has no right, for it will come in the matn there: “It is valid for the building and trees: if the term expires, he removes them and delivers the land empty, unless the lessor compensates him for their value in a removed state and takes ownership, or he agrees to leave them, in which case the building and trees are for one party and the land for the other.” And al-Khayr al-Ramlī gave fatwa according to that, and sometimes he gave fatwa according to the first view out of consideration for the lessee due to preventing harm from him. His saying: (And if the first lease was at market rent, then its market rent increased, etc.) I say in al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd of the author of al-Hidāya: A man leased waqf land for three years with a known rent.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqā'iq, discusses the rulings concerning increases in rent for waqf (endowment) properties. The passage type is a collection of rulings (ruling_statement) with expansions and fatwa incidents. The author begins by stating the condition for the increase to be accepted: it must be a general increase from the community (ʿinda al-kull). If only one or two persons increase out of spite (taʿannutan), it is not accepted. Then the author summarizes the classification of the occupant: (1) if the occupant is not a lessee or is a lessee under a defective (fāsid) lease, he has no right and the increase is accepted, and the mutawalli hands the property to the new lessee; (2) if the occupant is a valid lessee, the increase is presented to him; if he accepts it, he has priority (huwa al-aḥaqq); otherwise, the mutawalli may lease to the second. Special rules apply for land with crops: if the land has crops planted by right (bi-ḥaqq), the increase is due from the first lessee from the time it occurred, and the delivery of past years and the named rent are due because the crop prevents a valid lease to another. If the crop is not by right (e.g., usurper or defective lease), it does not prevent validity. Then the author relates several fatwa incidents: (a) A lessee at market rent who subleases at a lower rent with glaring deficiency – the sublease is valid because the lessee owns the usufructs. (b) When market rent increases after the first lease, the increase is presented to the first lessee, not the second. (c) If the first lessee does not accept and the lease is rescinded, the second lease built on it is also rescinded. (d) If the mutawalli leases all parts together, an increase on some parts is not accepted because the consideration is the total rent. (e) Proof of increase due to market rent requires expert testimony. The passage then cites Qāḍīkhān's distinction between a deficiency that people tolerate (taghābun) – in which case the lease is valid and cannot be rescinded – and one they do not tolerate, in which case the lease is defective and the mutawalli can lease at market rent. If the first lease was at market rent and then market rent increases, the mutawalli may rescind. As long as he does not rescind, the named rent is due. Finally, a discussion about the priority of the first lessee after the term expires: he is not automatically entitled, except perhaps in cases where he has buildings or trees on the land and is willing to pay market rent, but there is disagreement, with some authorities giving him priority to prevent harm. The passage emphasizes that the Hanafi position relies on the principle that benefits owned by the lessee are like ownership, and that the mutawalli acts to protect the waqf.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghubn fāḥish): A glaring deficiency in the rent where the lessor is significantly underpaid, such that people would not normally tolerate it (lā yataghābanu al-nās fīhi).
حوادث الفتوى (hawādith al-fatwā): Judicial or fatwa incidents that have occurred and are recorded as precedents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa incident, what is the ruling if a lessee subleases waqf land at a rent with a glaring deficiency?
A) The sublease is void because it harms the waqf.
B) The sublease is valid because the lessee owns the usufruct.
C) The sublease is void unless the mutawalli approves.
D) The sublease is valid only if the sublessee also benefits the waqf.

Key Takeaway
Land with lawful crops prevents a new lease, and the lessee may sublease at a loss because he owns the usufruct.
