Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
5 min
Intra-Madhhab Dispute on Expert Witnesses for Market Rent
Intra-Hanafi dispute on number of expert witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of expert witnesses required to establish market value and evaluate the practical consequence.

Core Idea
Muhammad requires two expert witnesses to confirm market value; Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa hold that one trustworthy expert suffices.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq includes a citation from al-Khāniyya regarding the proof needed to verify that a sale or lease was at market value. The author relates an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Muhammad al-Shaybānī insists on two expert witnesses, while the other two (Abū Yūsuf and Abū Hanīfa) accept one. The practical difference affects the burden of proof in disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
How many expert witnesses are needed to prove that a prior lease or sale was at market value when an increase is claimed?
Analogized from the book of bequests on a guardian's sale of orphan's property.
2
State Muhammad's position
Muhammad requires two expert witnesses who agree on the value. If two agree, their statement is taken; a single expert is insufficient.
Reference: 'hādhā qawl Muḥammad Ammā ʿalā qawlihimā qawl al-wāḥid yakfī.'
3
State the position of the other two (Abū Yūsuf and Abū Hanīfa)
According to 'their saying' (qawlihimā), the testimony of one trustworthy expert is sufficient, analogous to tazkiya (witness accreditation).
The text says 'qawl al-wāḥid yakfī' as in tazkiya.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If one expert suffices, the mutawalli or guardian can more easily defend the transaction; if two are required, it is harder to prove the market value.
The judge's decision depends on which view is followed.
5
Note that the passage does not give a tarjih
The author of al-Bahr al-Rā'iq presents both views without preference, leaving the mufti to choose based on context.
In practice, later Hanafi works might prefer one view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرط الزيادة أن تكون عند الكل، أما لو زادها واحد أو اثنان تعنتاً فإنها غير مقبولة كما صرح به الأسبيجابي. وحاصل كلامهم في الزيادة أن الساكن لو كان غير مستأجر أو مستأجراً إجارة فاسدة فإنه لا حق له وتقبل الزيادة ويخرج ويسلم المتولي العين إلى المستأجر، وإن كان مستأجراً صحيحة، فإن كانت تعنتاً فهي غير مقبولة أصلاً، وإن كانت لزيادة أجر المثل عند الكل عرض المتولي الزيادة على المستأجر، فإن قبلها فهو الأحق وإلا آجرها من الثاني فإن كانت أرضاً فهي كغيرها لكن إن كانت الأرض خالية عن الزراعة أجرها للثاني وإلا وجبت الزيادة على المستأجر الأول من وقتها ووجب تسليم السنين الماضية والمسمى بحسابه قبلها لأن الزرع مانع من صحة الإجارة حيث كان مزروعاً بحق وهذا كذلك. وإن لم يكن مزروعاً بحق كالغاصب والمستأجر إجارة فاسدة فإنه لا يمنع صحة الإجارة كما في الظهيرية والسراجية لكونه لا يمنع التسليم، فإن كان المتولي مع قدرته على الرفع لا غرامة عليه وقد وقعت حوادث الفتوى منها : استأجر أرض الوقف بأجر المثل ثم أجرها لآخر بأقل بنقصان فاحش فأجبت بالصحة لأن المنافع المملوكة للمستأجر ليست كالوقف وإنما هي كالملك ولذا ملك الإعارة ومنها لو زاد أجر المثل بعد ما أجر المستأجر هل يعرض الأمر على الأول أم الثاني ؟ فأجبت على الأول لأنه المستأجر من المتولي. ومنها لو لم يقبل ونقضت وأجرها المتولي ممن زاد هل تنتقض الثانية؟ فأجبت تنتقض لكونها مبنية على الأولى فإذا انتقض الأصل انتقض ما ابتنى عليه كما في الفتاوى الصغرى من الإجارة الطويلة، وعلى هذا لو فسخت الأولى بخيار رؤية أو عيب بقضاء بطلت الثانية . ومنها لو أجر المتولي جميع جهات الوقف الخراجي والهلالي بأجرة المثل فزاد أجر مثل بعضها وزاد فيها غيره هل تؤجر من الآخر بعد العرض على الأول أو لا؟ فأجبت ينبغي أن لا تقبل الزيادة لأنه حيث استأجر الجميع إجارة واحدة إنما ينظر إلى زيادة أجرة الجميع لا كل واحدة. ومنها أنه كيف يعلم القاضي أن الزيادة بسبب زيادة أجر المثل؟ وهل يحتاج إلى إثبات ذلك؟ قلت : نعم لما في الخانية من كتاب الوصايا وصي باع شيئاً من مال اليتيم ثم طلب منه بأكثر مما باع فإن القاضي يرجع إلى أهل البصر؛ إن أخبره اثنان من أهل البصر والأمانة أنه باع بقيمته وإن قيمته ذلك فإن القاضي لا يلتفت إلى من يريد، وإن كان في المزايدة يشتري بأكثر وفي السوق بأقل لا ينتقض بيع الوصي لأجل تلك الزيادة بل يرجع إلى أهل البصر والأمانة، وإن اجتمع رجلان منهم على شيء يؤخذ بقولهما معاً، وهذا قول محمد، أما على قولهما قول الواحد يكفي كما في التزكية ونحوها وعلى هذا قيم الوقف إذا أجر مستغل الوقف وجاء آخر يزيد في الأجرة .اهـ. وصرح قاضيخان من كتاب الإجارة بأنه إذا أجر بأقل من أجرة المثل ؛ فإن كان بنقصان يتغابن الناس فيه فهي صحيحة وليس للمتولي فسخها، وإن كان بنقصان لا يتغابن الناس فيه فهي فاسدة وله أن يؤاجرها إجارة صحيحة إما من الأول أو من غيره بأجر المثل وبالزيادة على قدر ما يرضى به المستأجر، فإن سكن المستأجر الأول وجب أجر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ وعليه الفتوى وإن كانت الإجارة الأولى بأجرة المثل ثم ازداد أجر مثله كان للمتولي أن يفسخ الإجارة، وما لم يفسخ كان على المستأجر الأجر المسمى اهـ. وفي الحاوي: ويفتي بالضمان في غصب عقار الوقف وغصب منافعه، وكذا كل ما بيده إلى انتهاء والغراس وهي مسألة الأرض المحتكرة لأن في إبقائها بيده دفع الضرر عنه مع عدم ضرر الوقف على أن في هذه الصورة كلاماً فإن مقتضى إطلاق المتون في كتاب الإجارة يدل على أنه لاحق له فإنه سيأتي في المتن هناك قوله : وصح للبناء والغراس فإن مضت المدة قلعهما وسلمها فارغة إلا أن يغرم له المؤجر قيمته مقلوعاً ويتملكه أو يرضى بتركه فيكون البناء والغراس لهذا والأرض لهذا .اهـ. وقد أفتى بذلك الخير الرملي وتارة أفتى I answered that it is valid because the benefits owned by the lessee are not like the endowment; rather they are like ownership, hence he has the right to give it as a loan. I answered: to the first, because he is the lessee from the mutawalli. I answered: it is rescinded because it is built upon the first; if the origin is rescinded, what is built upon it is rescinded, as in al-Fatāwā al-Ṣughrā regarding long leases. And similarly, if the first lease is rescinded due to option of sighting or defect by court ruling, the second is void. I said: Yes, because in al-Khāniyya from the book of bequests: if a guardian sold something from the orphan's property, then someone sought it from him at a higher price, the judge refers to experts; if two experts of sight and trust inform him that he sold it at its value and that its value is that, the judge does not pay attention to the one who wants more, even if there is a bidder at a higher price and in the market it is lower. The sale of the guardian is not rescinded due to that increase; rather, reference is made to experts of sight and trust. If two of them agree on something, both statements are taken together. This is the saying of Muḥammad. As for their saying (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad?), the statement of one is sufficient, as in matters of tazkiya and the like. Based on this, the same applies if the mutawalli of the endowment leases the income-generating endowment and another comes to increase the rent, etc. And Qāḍīkhān explicitly stated in the book of leases that if he leases at less than market rent, then if it is a deficiency in which people engage in mutual toleration (taghābun), it is valid and the mutawalli does not have the right to rescind it. And if it is a deficiency in which people do not engage in mutual toleration, it is legally defective (fāsid) and he may lease it validly, either from the first or from another, at market rent and at an increase to the extent that the lessee agrees. If the first lessee occupies, the market rent is due, no matter how high, and the fatwa is upon this. And if the first lease was at market rent, then its market rent increased, the mutawalli may rescind the lease, and as long as he does not rescind, the named rent is incumbent on the lessee. And in al-Ḥāwī: It is fatwa that liability (ḍamān) applies in usurpation of waqf real estate and usurpation of its usufructs, and similarly everything in his possession until the end of its term. As for when the term expires, what is the basis for his having more right to lease than others? Yes, he may have more right by another cause, namely if the leased land has a building or trees on it or the like, and he agrees to pay market rent for the land empty of the building and trees. This is the issue of the leased land (al-arḍ al-muḥtakara), because keeping it in his possession prevents harm to him without harm to the endowment. However, there is discussion about this scenario, because the absolute wording of the matn in the book of leases indicates that he has no right, for it will come in the matn there: “It is valid for the building and trees: if the term expires, he removes them and delivers the land empty, unless the lessor compensates him for their value in a removed state and takes ownership, or he agrees to leave them, in which case the building and trees are for one party and the land for the other.” And al-Khayr al-Ramlī gave fatwa according to that, and sometimes he gave fatwa according to the first view out of consideration for the lessee due to preventing harm from him. His saying: (And if the first lease was at market rent, then its market rent increased, etc.) I say in al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd of the author of al-Hidāya: A man leased waqf land for three years with a known rent.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqā'iq, discusses the rulings concerning increases in rent for waqf (endowment) properties. The passage type is a collection of rulings (ruling_statement) with expansions and fatwa incidents. The author begins by stating the condition for the increase to be accepted: it must be a general increase from the community (ʿinda al-kull). If only one or two persons increase out of spite (taʿannutan), it is not accepted. Then the author summarizes the classification of the occupant: (1) if the occupant is not a lessee or is a lessee under a defective (fāsid) lease, he has no right and the increase is accepted, and the mutawalli hands the property to the new lessee; (2) if the occupant is a valid lessee, the increase is presented to him; if he accepts it, he has priority (huwa al-aḥaqq); otherwise, the mutawalli may lease to the second. Special rules apply for land with crops: if the land has crops planted by right (bi-ḥaqq), the increase is due from the first lessee from the time it occurred, and the delivery of past years and the named rent are due because the crop prevents a valid lease to another. If the crop is not by right (e.g., usurper or defective lease), it does not prevent validity. Then the author relates several fatwa incidents: (a) A lessee at market rent who subleases at a lower rent with glaring deficiency – the sublease is valid because the lessee owns the usufructs. (b) When market rent increases after the first lease, the increase is presented to the first lessee, not the second. (c) If the first lessee does not accept and the lease is rescinded, the second lease built on it is also rescinded. (d) If the mutawalli leases all parts together, an increase on some parts is not accepted because the consideration is the total rent. (e) Proof of increase due to market rent requires expert testimony. The passage then cites Qāḍīkhān's distinction between a deficiency that people tolerate (taghābun) – in which case the lease is valid and cannot be rescinded – and one they do not tolerate, in which case the lease is defective and the mutawalli can lease at market rent. If the first lease was at market rent and then market rent increases, the mutawalli may rescind. As long as he does not rescind, the named rent is due. Finally, a discussion about the priority of the first lessee after the term expires: he is not automatically entitled, except perhaps in cases where he has buildings or trees on the land and is willing to pay market rent, but there is disagreement, with some authorities giving him priority to prevent harm. The passage emphasizes that the Hanafi position relies on the principle that benefits owned by the lessee are like ownership, and that the mutawalli acts to protect the waqf.

Key Terms
تزكية (tazkiya): The process of accrediting a witness as trustworthy.
أهل البصر والأمانة (ahl al-baṣr wa al-amāna): Individuals with expertise (sight/knowledge) and trustworthiness; i.e., expert witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is Muhammad's requirement regarding expert witnesses for proving market value?
A) One expert witness suffices.
B) Two expert witnesses who agree are required.
C) Three expert witnesses are required.
D) Written evidence is required instead of witnesses.

Key Takeaway
Muhammad requires two expert witnesses to prove market value; Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa accept one, and the passage gives no tarjih.

Nullification of a Dependent Lease When the Primary Lease Falls
Question and answer about automatic nullification of dependent lease

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a second lease built upon a first lease is nullified when the first is nullified, and identify the qiyas that supports this ruling.

Core Idea
A lease dependent on another is like a building on a foundation – if the foundation falls, the building falls.

In this lesson, we examine a fatwa from Ibn Nujaym regarding the effect of nullification of a lease on a subsequent dependent lease. The mutawalli (trustee) of a waqf may lease the property in a sequence where the second lease is conditional upon the first. The question arises: if the first lease is nullified, does the second automatically become void? The author provides a clear ruling based on the principle of dependency (mabniyyah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a second lease made by the mutawalli after the first lease was nullified. The ruling: it is nullified (batil).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas (analogy) from the principle cited in al-Fatawa al-Sughra: when the original is nullified, what is built upon it is nullified.
The dalil is a general legal analogy, not a direct textual source.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The analogy is based on the dependency of the second lease on the first, like a building on a foundation. This is a clear (jaliy) qiyas.
Dependency (mabniyyah) is the effective cause (illa).
4
Note the extension
The same ruling applies if the first lease is rescinded by a judge due to khiyar al-ru'yah (option of inspection) or a defect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المتولي. ومنها لو لم يقبل ونقضت وأجرها المتولي ممن زاد هل تنتقض الثانية؟ فأجبت تنتقض لكونها مبنية على الأولى فإذا انتقض الأصل انتقض ما ابتنى عليه كما في الفتاوى الصغرى من الإجارة الطويلة، وعلى هذا لو فسخت الأولى بخيار رؤية أو عيب بقضاء بطلت الثانية.
The trustee. And among them: if he did not accept and it was nullified, and the trustee leased to someone who increased, is the second nullified? I answered: It is nullified because it is built upon the first. When the original is nullified, what is built upon it is nullified, as in al-Fatawa al-Sughra regarding long-term lease. And upon this, if the first is rescinded due to option of inspection or defect by court ruling, the second becomes void.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof, presented as a question-and-answer. The author, Ibn Nujaym, addresses a scenario: a trustee (mutawalli) initially leases a waqf property, then that lease is nullified for some reason (perhaps due to a defect or lack of acceptance). Subsequently, the trustee leases the same property to another person who offers a higher rent. The question is whether the second lease is automatically nullified when the first is invalidated. The author answers affirmatively, on the principle that the second lease is built upon the first (mabniyyah 'ala al-ula). When the foundation (the first lease) is nullified, the structure built upon it also falls. He cites al-Fatawa al-Sughra (the Smaller Fatwas) as authority for this principle in the context of long-term leases (ijarah tawilah). He then extends the ruling: if the first lease is rescinded by a judge due to a contractual defect (e.g., option of inspection or defect), the second lease is also void. The legal reasoning is based on analogy (qiyas): the dependency of the second lease on the first is akin to a building on a foundation.

Key Terms
المتولي (al-mutawallī): The trustee or administrator of a waqf (endowment) appointed to manage its affairs.
الإجارة الطويلة (al-ijārah al-ṭawīlah): A long-term lease; the principle cited is that a dependent lease is nullified if the primary lease is nullified.
خيار الرؤية (khiyār al-ruʾyah): The option of inspection: the right to rescind a contract after seeing the object if it differs from description.
مبنية على الأولى (mabniyyah 'ala al-ula): Built upon the first; indicating legal dependency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a trustee leases a waqf property, then the first lease is nullified due to a defect, and the trustee had already leased it to another person, what happens to the second lease?
A) The second lease remains valid because it was made after the nullification.
B) The second lease is nullified because it was built upon the first.
C) The second lease is unaffected if the new lessee paid a higher rent.
D) The second lease becomes valid only if the judge confirms it.

Key Takeaway
A lease that is built upon another is inevitably nullified when the primary lease is nullified, protecting the integrity of the contractual chain.

Leasing All Waqf Properties Together: Partial Increase Does Not Cancel
Ruling that partial increase does not justify breaking a unitary lease

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a partial increase in rent for some components of a unitary lease does not justify cancellation, and explain the reasoning based on the integrity of the single contract.

Core Idea
Partial increase in rent for some parts does not break a single lease; only total rent increase matters.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling in waqf leasing. When a trustee leases all properties together as one unit, can a later rent increase for some properties justify canceling the lease? The answer protects contract stability and prevents piecemeal rescission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the lease structure
The trustee leased all categories of waqf (kharaji and hilali) together as one contract (ijarah wahidah). The initial rent was at the market rate (ajar al-mithl).
The unity of the contract is key.
2
Identify the subsequent event
Later, the market rent for some parts increased, and a new party offered a higher rent for those parts. The trustee wonders whether to accept this new offer after giving the first lessee the chance to match.
3
Apply the ruling
The author rules that the increase should not be accepted. The lease remains valid and binding. The reason is that the contract is a single unit; only the total rent change matters, not partial changes.
The legal principle: 'al-ijarah al-wahidah la tantahidh bi ziyadat ba'diha'.
4
Understand the rationale
If partial increases could justify cancellation, a tenant could lose parts of the leased property, and the integrity of the original agreement would be undermined. This ruling protects the lessee's stability and the trustee's duty to manage the waqf effectively.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها لو أجر المتولي جميع جهات الوقف الخراجي والهلالي بأجرة المثل فزاد أجر مثل بعضها وزاد فيها غيره هل تؤجر من الآخر بعد العرض على الأول أو لا؟ فأجبت ينبغي أن لا تقبل الزيادة لأنه حيث استأجر الجميع إجارة واحدة إنما ينظر إلى زيادة أجرة الجميع لا كل واحدة.
And among them: if the trustee leased all categories of waqf, both kharaji and hilali, at the market rent, then the market rent of some of them increased, and someone else increased (the bid) for them, should they be leased from the other after offering to the first? I answered: It is not appropriate to accept the increase because since he leased all as a single lease, consideration is given to the increase of the entire rent, not each individual one.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the author. The issue concerns a waqf that has multiple 'categories' (jihāt) — probably different types or locations of properties. The trustee leases them all together in one contract at a fair market rent. Later, the market rent for some of these properties rises, and another party offers a higher rent for just those parts. The question is whether the trustee can break the original contract to lease those parts to the new offeror. The author rules that the increase should not be accepted because the original lease was a single, unitary contract (ijarah wahidah). The only relevant factor is whether the total rent for the whole package has increased; a partial increase in some components does not justify nullifying the lease. The opposite view would allow piecemeal cancellation, which undermines the integrity of the original contract.

Key Terms
الوقف الخراجي (al-waqf al-kharājī): A waqf that generates revenue (kharaj) for public benefit, often agricultural land.
الوقف الهلالي (al-waqf al-hilālī): A waqf designated for specific charitable purposes, possibly for family or specific beneficiaries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A trustee leases three waqf shops together as one contract at market rent. The market rent for one shop doubles. What is the ruling?
A) The trustee must cancel the entire contract and re-lease.
B) The trustee can cancel only for that one shop.
C) The lease remains valid; the trustee cannot cancel due to partial increase.
D) The trustee must increase the rent for that one shop only.

Key Takeaway
A single lease cannot be broken for a partial rent increase; only the total rent matters.

Proving Increase in Market Rent: Expert Witnesses
Explanation of proving market rent increase via expert witnesses, with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi ruling on proving market rent increase, state the intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of expert witnesses, and apply the qiyas from orphan property to waqf.

Core Idea
Proof of market rent increase requires expert testimony; Imam Muhammad requires two, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf accept one.

This passage addresses a practical question: how does a judge know that an increase in rent reflects a genuine market change? The author draws from the law of guardianship over orphans, where expert witnesses are consulted to determine fair value. Within the Hanafi school, there is a key disagreement: does one expert suffice or must there be two? Understanding this dispute helps clarify the school's approach to proof in financial matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal question
What does the passage set out to determine? The judge needs to know if a rent increase is due to market conditions.
2
Extract the qiyas from orphan property
How does the case of the executor selling orphan's property establish the need for experts? The judge refers to ahl al-basr.
This is a qiyas jaliy: the asl is the executor case, the far' is the mutawalli leasing waqf property.
3
State the position of Imam Muhammad
According to Imam Muhammad, how many experts are needed? Two, based on the text from al-Khaniyya where two experts are mentioned.
4
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
They accept one expert, analogizing to tazkiyah (character testimony) where one suffices.
5
Apply to waqf
How does this dispute manifest in the leasing of waqf property? The mutawalli must present expert witnesses; the number depends on which view the qadi follows.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أنه كيف يعلم القاضي أن الزيادة بسبب زيادة أجر المثل؟ وهل يحتاج إلى إثبات ذلك؟ قلت : نعم لما في الخانية من كتاب الوصايا وصي باع شيئاً من مال اليتيم ثم طلب منه بأكثر مما باع فإن القاضي يرجع إلى أهل البصر؛ إن أخبره اثنان من أهل البصر والأمانة أنه باع بقيمته وإن قيمته ذلك فإن القاضي لا يلتفت إلى من يريد، وإن كان في المزايدة يشتري بأكثر وفي السوق بأقل لا ينتقض بيع الوصي لأجل تلك الزيادة بل يرجع إلى أهل البصر والأمانة، وإن اجتمع رجلان منهم على شيء يؤخذ بقولهما معاً، وهذا قول محمد، أما على قولهما قول الواحد يكفي كما في التزكية ونحوها وعلى هذا قيم الوقف إذا أجر مستغل الوقف وجاء آخر يزيد في الأجرة .اهـ.
And among them: how does the judge know that the increase is due to an increase in the market rent? And is proof needed for that? I said: Yes, as in al-Khaniyya from the book of wills: an executor sold something from an orphan's property, then demanded from him more than what he sold for; then the judge refers to experts. If two experts of insight and trustworthiness inform him that he sold at its value and that its value was that, then the judge does not pay attention to the one who wants (to increase). And if in the auction someone buys at a higher price and in the market it is lower, the executor's sale is not nullified due to that increase; rather, the judge refers to the experts. And if two experts agree on something, their statement is taken together. This is the saying of Muhammad. As for the view of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the statement of one suffices, as in tazkiyah and similar matters. And upon this, the waqf valuator, if he leases the waqf's productive property and someone comes offering more in rent... end.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage first presents the question: how can a judge determine whether an increase in rent is due to a genuine rise in market value? The author confirms that proof is required and draws an analogy from the law of guardianship (wilayah) over orphans. In al-Khaniyya, it is recorded: if a guardian (wasi) sells property of an orphan, and later someone claims the sale was undervalued, the judge must consult experts (ahl al-basr). If two reliable experts testify that the sale was at fair value, the judge ignores the claimant. Similarly, if an auction price is higher but market price lower, the guardian's sale stands. Then the author notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Imam Muhammad, two experts are required; according to the other two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), one expert suffices, analogous to tazkiyah (character witness). The author applies this to waqf: the mutawalli or valuator (qayyim al-waqf) leasing waqf property must have proof of market increase from at least two experts according to one view, or one according to another.

Key Terms
أهل البصر (ahl al-baṣr): People of insight and expertise, i.e., expert witnesses who can assess market value.
التزكية (al-tazkiyah): Character testimony; in legal procedure, testimony about the reliability of witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, how many expert witnesses are needed to prove that the market rent has increased for a waqf property?
A) None, the judge can rely on common knowledge.
B) One expert witness suffices.
C) Two expert witnesses are required.
D) Only the mutawalli's statement is accepted.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires proof by expert witnesses to establish market rent increase, with an internal dispute on the number of witnesses needed.

Leasing Below Market Rent: Negligible vs. Significant Deficiency
Ruling from Qadi Khan on lease validity below market rent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a negligible and significant deficiency in lease rent and state the Hanafi ruling for each scenario.

Core Idea
A lease below market rent is valid if the deficiency is negligible; if significant, it is fasid and market rent becomes due.

When a waqf trustee leases property below the market rate, is the lease automatically invalid? Not necessarily. Hanafi fiqh considers the magnitude of the deficiency, using the customary standard of what people overlook (yataghāban al-nās fīhi). This lesson unpacks Qadi Khan's ruling, which balances protecting waqf interests with contractual stability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Recognize that the ruling applies to a trustee (mutawalli) leasing a waqf property at a rent below the prevailing market rate (ujrat al-mithl).
2
Distinguish the two deficiency types
Determine whether the shortfall is negligible (people customarily overlook it) or significant (people would not overlook it). This is a factual, customary assessment.
The Arabic term 'yataghāban al-nās fīhi' is the benchmark.
3
State the ruling for each type
If negligible, the lease is sahih (valid) and the trustee cannot cancel. If significant, the lease is fasid (invalid) and the trustee may re-lease validly.
A fasid lease does not automatically terminate; the trustee has an option.
4
Determine the consequence of occupation
If the tenant occupies under a fasid lease, the tenant must pay the full ujrat al-mithl (market rent), regardless of the agreed amount.
This is wajib (obligatory) per the fatwa.
5
Identify the fatwa authority
The author states 'wa alayhi al-fatwa' (upon this is the fatwa), indicating this is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.
Qadi Khan is a later authority; his ruling is from fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصرح قاضيخان من كتاب الإجارة بأنه إذا أجر بأقل من أجرة المثل ؛ فإن كان بنقصان يتغابن الناس فيه فهي صحيحة وليس للمتولي فسخها، وإن كان بنقصان لا يتغابن الناس فيه فهي فاسدة وله أن يؤاجرها إجارة صحيحة إما من الأول أو من غيره بأجر المثل وبالزيادة على قدر ما يرضى به المستأجر، فإن سكن المستأجر الأول وجب أجر المثل بالغاً ما بلغ وعليه الفتوى
Qadi Khan stated in the book of Ijara: if he leased for less than the market rent, then if it is a deficiency that people overlook (taghabun), it is valid and the trustee cannot cancel it. And if it is a deficiency that people do not overlook, then it is invalid (fasid), and he may lease it validly either from the first lessee or from someone else at the market rent or with an increase that the lessee agrees to. If the first lessee occupies (the property), then the market rent is obligatory regardless of amount, and upon this is the fatwa.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from Qadi Khan, a prominent Hanafi jurist. It addresses a situation where a trustee (mutawalli) leases a waqf property at a rent below the prevailing market rate (ujrat al-mithl). The ruling distinguishes between two types of deficiency: a negligible deficiency that people customarily overlook (yutaghaban al-nas fihi) — such as a small difference that does not indicate negligence — and a significant deficiency that people would not overlook. In the first case, the lease is valid (sahih) and the trustee cannot cancel it. In the second, the lease is defective (fasid) and the trustee has the right to re-lease the property validly, either by renewing with the original lessee at the proper rent or by leasing to someone else at market rate. If the original lessee has already occupied the property under the fasid lease, he must pay the full market rent (ujrat al-mithl) regardless of the agreed amount. The author adds that this is the relied-upon position (wa 'alayhi al-fatwa). This ruling balances the interests of the waqf (ensuring fair return) with the principle that minor errors should not invalidate contracts.

Key Terms
يتغابن الناس فيه (yataghāban al-nās fīhi): A deficiency that people customarily overlook as negligible in business transactions.
أجر المثل (ujrat al-mithl): Market rent – the prevailing rental value for similar property in the same location.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A trustee leases a waqf land for 100 when the market rent is 150. People in the area consider 50 a significant difference. The tenant occupies the land. What is the ruling?
A) The lease is valid; the tenant pays 100.
B) The lease is fasid; the tenant must pay 150 for the period of occupation.
C) The lease is batil; the tenant must vacate without paying anything.
D) The lease is valid but the trustee can cancel at any time.

Key Takeaway
A lease below market rent is not automatically invalid; the key is whether the deficiency is negligible according to custom.

Trustee's Right to Cancel Lease on Market Rent Increase
Ruling from Qadi Khan on trustee's right to cancel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule regarding the trustee's right to cancel a waqf lease when market rent increases and explain the binding nature of the named rent until cancellation.

Core Idea
The trustee may cancel a lease if market rent rises, but until cancellation the lessee pays only the agreed rent.

This short passage from Qadi Khan addresses a critical issue in waqf management: balancing the trustee's duty to maximize endowment revenue against the sanctity of contracts. It clarifies that the trustee has an option to rescind a lease when market conditions improve, but the lessee is not automatically liable for the higher rate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial lease terms
The trustee leased the waqf property at the prevailing market rent (ujrat al-mithl). This is a valid lease at a fair price.
2
Identify the change in market conditions
Over time, the market rent for similar properties increases. This creates a potential loss for the waqf if the lease continues unchanged.
3
Determine the trustee's right
The trustee has the right (khiyar) to cancel (faskh) the existing lease. This is a discretionary right, not an obligation.
The right is justified by the need to protect the waqf's interests.
4
Determine the lessee's obligation before cancellation
Until the trustee actually cancels the lease, the lessee remains liable only for the originally agreed rent (al-ajr al-musamma), not the higher market rate.
The contract remains binding until formally rescinded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كانت الإجارة الأولى بأجرة المثل ثم ازداد أجر مثله كان للمتولي أن يفسخ الإجارة، وما لم يفسخ كان على المستأجر الأجر المسمى اهـ.
And if the first lease was at the market rent, then its market rent increased, the trustee may cancel the lease, and as long as he does not cancel, the lessee is liable for the named rent.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This is a concise ruling from Qadi Khan. It addresses a different scenario: the trustee initially leased the property at the prevailing market rent (ujrat al-mithl). Over time, the market rent increases. The trustee is given the right to cancel (faskh) the existing lease. However, until he exercises this right, the lessee remains obligated to pay only the originally agreed rent (al-ajr al-musamma), not the higher market rate. This ruling reflects the principle that the lease contract is honored until it is formally rescinded. The trustee's right to cancel is justified by the need to protect the waqf's interests, ensuring that the endowment continues to generate optimal revenue. This is a key ruling in waqf management and is subject to further refinement (e.g., the 'fahisha' condition) discussed in subsequent passages.

Key Terms
الأجر المسمى (al-ajr al-musammā): The named or agreed-upon rent in the lease contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A trustee leases a waqf land at market rent of 100. After one year, market rent rises to 150. The trustee has not yet cancelled the lease. What rent must the lessee pay?
A) 150
B) 100
C) The average of 100 and 150
D) Nothing until the trustee cancels

Key Takeaway
The trustee may cancel a waqf lease if market rent increases, but the lessee remains bound by the original rent until cancellation.

Exorbitant Increase and Waqf Lease Cancellation
Critical refinement of the condition for lease cancellation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify what constitutes an exorbitant increase (al-ziyadah al-fahishah) in waqf lease and state the condition under which cancellation is permitted according to Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Only an exorbitant increase—double or what people deem significant—justifies cancelling a waqf lease.

This passage refines a ruling from al-Hidayah about the cancellation of waqf leases due to a rise in market rent. The author clarifies that not every increase matters; only an exorbitant one, defined by custom as doubling or beyond, triggers the right to nullify. He analogizes to the rule for deficient rent: a minor deviation is overlooked. Understanding this condition preserves the stability of contracts while protecting the perpetual benefit of waqf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Locate the statement from al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid: a lease of waqf land may be cancelled if the market rent increases exorbitantly. Note the key expression 'al-ziyadah al-fahishah'.
The base ruling allows cancellation, but only under a specific condition.
2
Define 'exorbitant increase'
The author defines fahishah as doubling or more of the original rent, or what people customarily do not overlook. Understand that 'taghabun' (overlooking) is the benchmark.
Minor increases (e.g., 1 in 10) are neglected; the lease remains binding.
3
Recognize the analogical reasoning
The author draws an analogy to the case of deficiency: a small shortfall from market rent (yasir) does not invalidate the lease, just as a small increase does not permit cancellation. The same 'taghabun' standard applies.
This symmetry in increase and decrease shows consistent principle.
4
Apply the rule to an example
Work through the given example: a house rented for 10, market rent increases to 11 (a 10% rise). This is not exorbitant, so no cancellation. Compare with a rise to 20 or more, which triggers the option.
The author stresses that even a two-dirham difference in both directions may be overlooked if custom deems it negligible.
5
Note the conflicting narrations
Although not fully detailed here, the author implies two intra-Hanafi views: one allowing cancellation on any rent increase, and the other restricting it to exorbitant. The author sides with the refined view requiring fahishah.
The disagreement is over the threshold, not the principle of cancellation itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أقول في التجنيس والمزيد لصاحب الهداية رجل استأجر أرض وقف ثلاث سنين بأجرة معلومة . ثم قال: فإذا زاد أجر مثل تلك الأرض زيادة فاحشة بأن صارت أجرتها ضعف ما كانت أو أكثر فإن للإجارة أن تنقض عند الزيادة الفاحشة نظراً للوقف وصيانة لحق الله تعالى وإبقاء للخيرات .اهـ. وتقييده بالفاحشة يدل على عدم نقضها باليسير ولعل المراد بالفاحشة ما لا يتغابن الناس فيها كما في طرف النقصان فإنه جائز عن أجر المثل إذا كان يسيراً والواحد في العشرة يتغابن الناس فيه كما ذكروه في كتاب الوكالة، وهذا قيد حسن يجب حفظه، فإذا كانت أجرة دار عشرة مثلاً وزاد أجر مثلها واحداً فإنها لا تنقض لو أجرها المتولي بتسعة فإنها لا تنقض بخلاف الدرهمين في الطرفين، ويجوز النقصان المثل نقصاً فاحشاً للضرورة
I say in al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid of the author of al-Hidayah: A man leased a waqf land for three years at a known rent. Then he said: 'If the market rent of that land increases with an exorbitant increase, such that its rent becomes double what it was or more, then the lease may be nullified due to the exorbitant increase, out of consideration for the waqf and to protect the right of Allah Almighty and to preserve charitable endowments.' End of quote. And his restricting to 'exorbitant' indicates that it is not nullified by a small increase. Perhaps what is meant by exorbitant is that which people do not overlook, as in the case of deficiency; for it is permissible to accept a deficiency from market rent if it is small, and one in ten is something people overlook, as they mentioned in the book of agency. This is a good restriction that must be remembered. So if the rent of a house is, for example, ten, and its market rent increases by one, then it is not nullified, just as if the trustee leased it for nine, it is not nullified. In contrast, two dirhams in both directions (increase and decrease?) qualifies. And it is permissible to have a deficiency of the like of an exorbitant deficiency out of necessity.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from the author commenting on a statement from al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid by the author of al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani). The quote states that a lease of waqf land may be nullified if the market rent increases 'exorbitantly' (fahisha), specifically defined as doubling or more. The author clarifies that this condition prevents nullification for minor increases. He analogizes to the case of deficiency (naqsan): just as a small shortfall from market rent does not invalidate the lease, a small increase does not justify cancellation. He gives an example: if the rent is ten and increases by one, the lease stands. The standard is whether people would generally overlook such a difference (taghabun). The author endorses this as a good restriction. The passage also notes that an exorbitant deficiency may be permissible out of necessity. This discussion sets the stage for the conflicting narrations that follow in the original text (particularly the two views: one allowing cancellation for any increase in market rent, the other disallowing it).

Key Terms
الزيادة الفاحشة (al-ziyādah al-fāḥishah): An exorbitant increase in market rent, generally considered by scholars as doubling or more, or what people do not overlook.
يتغابن الناس فيه (yataghāban al-nās fīhi): An amount that people customarily overlook in transactions, considered negligible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Whether the price of a leased property is fair.
B) Whether an increase in rent is considered exorbitant or minor.
C) Whether a lease is valid for more than three years.
D) Whether the mutawalli has the authority to lease.

Key Takeaway
A waqf lease can only be cancelled due to a rent increase if that increase is exorbitant (fahish), defined as doubling or more, or what people do not overlook; minor increases are neglected and the lease remains binding.

Definition of Fahish Increase in Waqf Lease
Defines fāḥish increase threshold for rescinding waqf lease.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define fāḥish increase in a waqf lease and apply the customary threshold to determine whether rescission is permitted.

Core Idea
A waqf lease is rescinded only for increases that people do not overlook.

This lesson introduces the key concept of 'fāḥish' (excessive) increase in the context of waqf leases. The Hanafi school sets a flexible yet principled threshold based on custom: minor, commonly overlooked differences are tolerated, but anything beyond that may trigger rescission to protect the endowment. Understanding this definition is essential for mutawallīs and judges dealing with waqf property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is rescinding a waqf lease due to a rise in market rent. The ruling is that rescission is permitted only when the increase is fāḥish.
The passage explicitly restricts rescission to fāḥish increase.
2
Define the key term fāḥish
The passage defines fāḥish as 'what people do not overlook in mutual transactions' (ma lā yataghāban al-nās fīhā). This is a customary standard, not a fixed percentage.
Analogous to the definition in the Book of Agency.
3
Apply the threshold to examples
If the market rent increases by 1 dirham on 10 (10%), this is overlooked and does not justify rescission. A difference of 2 dirhams (20%) is not overlooked and is fāḥish.
The passage uses the example of one dirham in ten as overlooked.
4
Note the exception for necessity
A trustee may reduce rent excessively if necessary to secure a tenant, even if the decrease itself is fāḥish. This exception does not apply to increases.
Necessity overrides the usual restriction.
5
Consider the ikhtilaf among scholars
Some scholars define fāḥish as a fixed proportion (e.g., double the rent), but the relied-upon Hanafi view is the customary one endorsed by the author of al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq.
The passage affirms the customary definition as a 'good restriction that must be memorized'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للوقف فيما اختلف العلماء فيه حتى نقضت الإجارة عند الزيادة الفاحشة نظراً للوقف وصيانة لحق الله تعالى وإبقاء للخيرات .اهـ. وتقييده بالفاحشة يدل على عدم نقضها باليسير ولعل المراد بالفاحشة ما لا يتغابن الناس فيها كما في طرف النقصان فإنه جائز عن أجر المثل إذا كان يسيراً والواحد في العشرة يتغابن الناس فيه كما ذكروه في كتاب الوكالة، وهذا قيد حسن يجب حفظه، فإذا كانت أجرة دار عشرة مثلاً وزاد أجر مثلها واحداً فإنها لا تنقض لو أجرها المتولي بتسعة فإنها لا تنقض بخلاف الدرهمين في الطرفين، ويجوز النقصان المثل نقصاً فاحشاً للضرورة
Regarding the endowment, scholars differed about whether the lease is rescinded upon an excessive increase, out of consideration for the endowment, protection of the right of Allah, and preservation of charitable works. The restriction to excessive indicates that it is not rescinded for a slight increase. Perhaps what is meant by excessive is that concerning which people do not overlook mutual disparity, similar to the side of decrease: it is permissible for less than the market rent if it is slight, and one in ten is something people overlook, as they mentioned in the book of agency. This is a good restriction that must be memorized. So if the rent of a house was ten dirhams for example and the market rent increased by one, it is not rescinded if the trustee rented it for nine; it is not rescinded, contrary to two dirhams on both ends. And it is permissible to decrease below the market rent by an excessive decrease due to necessity.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the condition for rescinding a waqf lease due to an increase in market rent. It establishes that only an excessive (fāḥish) increase justifies rescission, not a trivial one. The author defines fāḥish as the amount people typically overlook in transactions, using the analogy of the slight decrease (naqṣān) in rent where a decrease by one dirham out of ten (10 to 9) is overlooked and thus does not invalidate the lease. Conversely, a disparity of two dirhams on both ends (e.g., 10 to 8 or 8 to 10) is not overlooked and would be considered excessive. An exception is made for necessity: a trustee may reduce the rent even excessively if needed. This lesson focuses on defining the threshold; the actual rescission process and ikhtilāf among scholars are covered in subsequent lessons.

Key Terms
فاحش (fāḥish): Excessive increase in waqf rent that people do not overlook; threshold based on custom.
غبن فاحش (ghabn fāḥish): Excessive disparity between rent and market value; analogous to fāḥish increase.
أجر المثل (ujr al-mithl): Fair market rent at the time of contract.
متولي الوقف (mutawallī al-waqf): Trustee or administrator of the waqf property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Any increase of more than 10% of the original rent.
B) An increase that is double the original rent.
C) An increase that people do not overlook in mutual transactions.
D) An increase that the trustee deems excessive.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of fāḥish increase in waqf lease is based on custom: only what people do not overlook triggers rescission.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Rescinding Waqf Lease Due to Demand Increase
Presents two riwayat on whether demand-driven rent increase justifies rescission, and discusses the definition of fāḥish increase.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi transmissions on rescinding a waqf lease due to demand increase and evaluate the practical consequence of each view.

Core Idea
Two equally strong Hanafi transmissions: one rescinds a waqf lease on demand increase, the other does not.

In this passage, you will encounter an intra-Hanafi dispute where two transmissions from later fatwa collections offer conflicting answers. Understanding why both are considered valid and how a judge may choose reveals the flexibility within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two transmissions
Name the two riwayāt presented: riwāyat Sharḥ al-Ṭaḥāwī and riwāyat Ahl Samarqand.
These are later fatwa collections, not the six core books.
2
State each transmission's ruling on rescission
Sharḥ al-Ṭaḥāwī: the lease is rescinded. Ahl Samarqand: the lease is not rescinded. Note the reasoning: Sharḥ al-Ṭaḥāwī says the lease renews periodically and waqf requires consideration; Samarqand says original rent was fair.
3
Identify the condition for rescission under Sharḥ al-Ṭaḥāwī
The rent must actually increase due to demand, not just a higher offer. Also, if there is an obstacle like unripe crops, the lease continues until removal, with market rent due from the time of increase.
The judge rescinds after proof by two upright experts.
4
Recognize the procedural and authoritative weight
If a Hanafi judge rules by Samarqand, it is binding. No other Hanafi may later rescind. If a non-Hanafi judge rules to disregard the increase, it is consensus.
The author notes both transmissions are close in strength.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In jurisdictions following Samarqand, leases are stable; in others, leases may be rescinded, forcing tenants to pay market rate or leave.
The author does not give a definitive tarjīḥ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم رأيت في رسالة العلامة قنلى زاده أن في مسألة زيادة أجر المثل زيادة فاحشة بزيادة الرغبات اختلف المشايخ؛ ففي رواية شرح الطحاوي تفسخ الإجارة السابقة لأن الإجارة تنعقد شيئاً فشيئاً والوقف يجب له النظر، وفي رواية فتاوى أهل سمرقند لا تفسخ قال : والنقول على ما ذكرنا كثيرة. ثم قال بعد سرد النقول من الطرفين: فتحرر من هذه النقول أن إجارة الوقف إن كان بغبن فاحش لم تصح ابتداء، وإن كان بأجر المثل أو بغبن يسير صحت، فإن لم تزدد الأجرة في نفس الأمر لكن جاء رجل وقبل الوقف بأجرة زائدة لا تفسخ الأولى بل لا بد من أن تزدد في نفس الأمر بزيادة الرغبات، ويثبت ذلك عند القاضي بخبر عدلين من أهل الخبرة أو واحد منهم يفسخ القاضي الإجارة، وإلى وقت الفسخ يجب المسمى الأول إن لم يكن في المأجور ما يمنع الفسخ كزرع لم يستحصد بعد، وإن كان فيه ذلك تبقى الإجارة إلى أن يزول لكن يجب أجر المثل من وقت الزيادة إلى أن يزول. هذا في رواية شرح الطحاوي، وفي رواية أهل سمرقند لا تفسخ بالزيادة العارضة إن وقعت على أجر المثل ابتداء، والروايتان قريبتان من التساوي في القوة والرجحان فإني لم أر الترجيح الصريح إلا فيما نقل في أنفع الوسائل عن فتاوى برهان الدين أنه يفتي بأن له أن يفسخ العقد لكن إذا ترافع المتولي والمستأجر الأول وأثبت زيادة الأجر بزيادة الرغبات لكن إن حكم الحاكم الحنفي برواية أهل سمرقند أو ترافعا إلى غير الحنفي فحكم بإلغاء اعتبار الزيادة العارضة كان مجمعاً عليه، وليس لحنفي آخر الفسخ ذاهباً إلى رواية شرح الطحاوي وهل المراد بقوله «تفسخ الإجارة إذا زادت الرغبات» أنه يفسخها القاضي بنفسه أو المتولي عند القاضي وبإذنه ويحكم القاضي بذلك؟ لم يحرره المتقدمون وإنما تعرض له الطرسوسي وجزم بالأول، وإنما يفسخ القاضي إذا امتنع الناظر عنه. اهـ. ملخصاً. قلت : وسيأتي قريباً عن الحاوي ترجيح رواية شرح الطحاوي .. قوله : ( ولعل المراد بالفاحشة الخ ذكر العلامة قنلى زاده عن الحاوي الحصيري أن الزيادة الفاحشة مقدرة بضعف الذي أجره أو لا ثم قال : وهذا قول لم نره لغيره والحق أن كل ما لا يتغابن الناس بمثله فهو زيادة فاحشة نصفاً كانت أو ربعاً وهو ما لا يدخل تحت تقويم المتقومين في المختار، ثم ردد أنه هل هذا روايتان أو مراد العامة أيضاً بالغبن الفاحش ما ذكر ؟ لم يحرره أحد قبلنا وعزى إلى الذخيرة مثل ما في الحاوي اهـ. ويؤيد ما في الحاوي ما قدمه المؤلف قبل صفحة عن القنية من قول بغبن فاحش نصف المثل ونحوه فإن الغبن مقابل الزيادة فاعتبر فيه النصف ونحوه فكذا في الزيادة .
Then I saw in the treatise of the distinguished scholar Qunali Zada that on the issue of market rent increasing excessively due to increased demand, the shaykhs differed: according to the transmission of Sharh al-Tahawi, the earlier lease is rescinded because the lease renews little by little and consideration for the waqf is obligatory. According to the transmission of the fatwas of the people of Samarqand, it is not rescinded. He said: the transmissions on what we have mentioned are many. Then after listing the transmissions from both sides he said: from these transmissions it is established that if the waqf lease involved excessive disparity it is not valid initially; if it was at market rent or with slight disparity it is valid. If the rent does not actually increase but a person comes and offers an increased rent for the waqf, the first lease is not rescinded; rather it is necessary that it actually increases due to increased demand, and this is established before the judge by the testimony of two upright experts or one of them, then the judge rescinds the lease. Up to the time of rescission the initially named rent is obligatory; if the leased property contains something preventing rescission, like unripe crops, the lease remains until that obstacle goes away, but market rent is obligatory from the time of the increase until the obstacle goes away. This is according to the transmission of Sharh al-Tahawi. According to the transmission of the people of Samarqand, it is not rescinded due to the incidental increase if it originated at market rent. The two transmissions are close to equal in strength and preponderance, for I have not seen explicit preponderance except what is transmitted in Anfa' al-Wasail from the fatwas of Burhan al-Din: he gave the fatwa that he may rescind the contract if the trustee and the first lessee litigate and prove the increase in rent due to increased demand. But if a Hanafi judge rules by the transmission of the people of Samarqand, or they litigate before a non-Hanafi and he rules to disregard the incidental increase, that is consensus. And it is not for another Hanafi to rescind, following the transmission of Sharh al-Tahawi. And what is meant by his statement 'the lease is rescinded if demand increases'? Is the judge himself rescinding or the trustee before the judge with his permission and the judge issues a ruling? The earlier scholars did not determine this; al-Tarsusi addressed it and decided the first. The judge only rescinds if the trustee declines. This is a summary. I said: soon from al-Hawi there is a preponderance of the transmission of Sharh al-Tahawi. His statement: 'Perhaps what is meant by fahish...' – Qunali Zada mentioned from al-Hawi al-Husayri that fahish increase is estimated at double the rent or not, then he said: this is a statement we have not seen from anyone else, and the truth is that whatever people do not overlook mutual disparity is a fahish increase, whether half or a quarter, and it is not subject to evaluation by appraisers in the preferred view. Then he doubted whether these are two transmissions or whether the general public also mean by fahish ghabn what we mentioned? No one before us determined this, and he attributed to al-Dhakhirah similar to what is in al-Hawi. And what is in al-Hawi is supported by what the author presented a page earlier from al-Qunya: the statement about fahish ghabn being half the like and similar, for ghabn is the opposite of increase, so half and similar are considered, and similarly for increase.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether an increase in market rent due to increased demand (ziyādat al-raghebat) justifies rescinding a waqf lease. Two transmissions (riwāyat) are presented: from Sharḥ al-Ṭaḥāwī, which upholds rescission reasoning that the lease renews periodically and the waqf's interest requires review; and from Fatāwā Ahl Samarqand, which rejects rescission. The author notes both are strong, but if a Hanafi judge rules by the Samarqandi view, it is binding and no other Hanafi can later rescind. He also discusses procedural details: proof before the judge, whether the trustee acts directly, and obstacles to rescission. The second part of the passage returns to the definition of fāḥish, citing al-Ḥāwī that it is what people do not overlook, rejecting a fixed fraction like half or double. This clarifies that the definition is custom-based, not arithmetic. The author gives no definitive tarjīḥ but notes the upcoming preponderance from al-Ḥāwī.

Key Terms
رواية شرح الطحاوي (riwāyat Sharḥ al-Ṭaḥāwī): One of two Hanafi transmissions on rescinding waqf lease for demand increase; rules in favor of rescission.
رواية أهل سمرقند (riwāyat Ahl Samarqand): The other transmission from the fatwas of Samarqand; rules against rescission.
زيادة الرغبات (ziyādat al-raghebat): Increase in market rent caused by higher demand, as opposed to intrinsic rise in value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition must be met for the lease to be rescinded under the transmission of Sharḥ al-Ṭaḥāwī?
A) Any increase in market rent after the contract.
B) The rent must have increased in fact due to increased demand, not just a higher offer.
C) The trustee must personally rescind the lease.
D) The lessee must agree to a higher rent.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains two equally strong transmissions on rescinding waqf leases due to demand increase, and a judge may adopt either.

Building on Waqf Land: When the Owner-Builder Must Remove or Stay
First scenario: building owner on waqf land and the rent assessment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a building owner on waqf land must remove his building if its presence prevents the land from being rented at a higher market rate, and may stay only if removal would not increase rent.

Core Idea
A building on waqf land is private property, but removal may be required if the waqf suffers financial loss from below-market rent.

This lesson presents the first ruling from al-Muhīṭ: a person owns a building on waqf land and wishes to rent the land. The trustee must compare the current rent with what the land would earn if the building were removed. If removal would allow a higher rent, the owner must demolish his building and the land is rented to another. Otherwise, he may remain at the current rent due to necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person owns a building on waqf land and wants to rent the land. The trustee must assess rent.
The building is private property owned by the lessee.
2
Assess the rent comparison
The trustee determines whether removing the building would allow the land to be rented for more than the current rent.
If removal yields higher rent, the waqf's interest demands it.
3
Apply the ruling: removal or stay
If removal increases rent, the owner must remove the building and the land is rented to another at the higher rate. If removal does not increase rent, the owner may stay at the current rent.
The principle: reducing rent below market is impermissible without necessity.
4
Understand the rationale
The text justifies the stay as necessity (darura) because forcing removal without benefit would cause harm.
This balances property rights and waqf interests.

قال في المحيط وغيره : حانوت وقف وعمارته ملك لرجل أبي صاحب العمارة أن يستأجر بأجر مثله ينظر ; إن كانت العمارة لو رفعت يستأجر بأكثر مما لأجره لا يستأجر صاحب العمارة كلف رفع العمارة ويؤجر من غيره لأن النقصان عن أجر المثل لا يجوز من غير ضرورة، وإن كان لا يستأجر بأكثر مما يستأجره لا يكلف ويترك في يده بذلك الأجر لأن فيه ضرورة .اهـ. فإن قلت : إذا استأجر أرض الوقف سنين على عقود كثيرة للبناء وحكم بصحتها ثم بنى فزاد إنسان عليه هل تنتقض الإجارة؟ قلت قال في المحيط وغيره : ولو استأجر أرضاً موقوفة وبنى فيها حانوتاً وسكنها فأراد غيره أن يزيد في الغلة ويخرجه من الحانوت ينظر؛ إن كانت أجرته مشاهرة إذا جاء رأس الشهر كان للقيم فسخ الإجارة لأن الإجارة إذا كانت مشاهرة تنعقد في رأس كل شهر ثم ينظر إن كان رفع البناء لا يضر بالوقف فله رفعه لأنه ملكه وإن كان يضر به فليس له رفعه لأنه وإن كان ملكه فليس له أن يضر بالوقف. ثم إن رضي المستأجر أن يتملكه القيم للوقف بالقيمة مبنياً أو منزوعاً أيهما ما كان أخف يتملكه القيم، وإن لم يرض لا يتملك لأن التملك بغير رضاه لا يجوز فيبقى إلى أن
He said in al-Muhit and others: A waqf shop and its building are owned by a man. The owner of the building may rent the land at its market rent. He looks: if removing the building would cause the land to be rented for more than its current rent, the owner of the building is required to remove the building and it is rented to someone else, because reducing below market rent is impermissible without necessity. If it would not be rented for more than its current rent, he is not required to remove it, and it is left in his hand at that rent because there is necessity. So if you say: if someone rents waqf land for years with multiple contracts for building and the contracts are ruled valid, then he builds, and then someone else increases the rent, is the lease rescinded? I reply: he said in al-Muhit and others: If someone rents waqf land and builds on it a shop and lives in it, and someone else wants to increase the produce and remove him from the shop, he looks: if his rent is monthly, when the end of the month comes, the administrator has the right to rescind the lease because if the lease is monthly it renews at the beginning of each month. Then he looks: if removing the building does not harm the waqf, he may remove it because it is his property; if it does harm the waqf, he may not remove it because although it is his property, he may not harm the waqf. Then if the lessee agrees that the administrator takes ownership for the waqf at the value, either built or dismantled, whichever is easier, the administrator takes ownership. If he does not agree, he does not take ownership because taking ownership without his consent is not permissible; it remains until...
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on buildings erected by a lessee on waqf land. It begins with a scenario from al-Muhīṭ: if a person owns a building on a waqf shop and wants to rent the land at market rent, the trustee must assess whether removing the building would allow renting the land at a higher rent. If so, the owner is compelled to remove his building to protect the waqf's interest. If not, he may stay at the current rent due to necessity. The passage then addresses a second scenario: a lessee builds on waqf land under a valid monthly lease, and a third party offers higher rent. The administrator may rescind at month-end if the lease is monthly. However, the building poses a problem: if it harms the waqf to remove it, the lessee cannot be forced to demolish it. The administrator may offer to purchase the building at market value, either standing or dismantled (whichever is cheaper for the waqf), but only if the lessee agrees. Without consent, the building remains, and the lessee continues to occupy, though details on rent follow in later text. This ruling balances the waqf's interest with the lessee's property rights, applying the maxim 'لا ضرر ولا ضرار' (no harm and no reciprocating harm).

Key Terms
عمارة الوقف (imārat al-waqf): Building constructed on waqf land by a lessee or owner of the building.
البناء بأمر المتولي (al-bināʾ bi-amr al-mutawallī): Building with the express permission of the trustee; then the building becomes part of the waqf? The passage quotes Abū al-Layth: if built with trustee's permission, building becomes waqf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Muhīṭ, when may a building owner on waqf land stay at the current rent despite it being below market?
A) Always, because the building is his property.
B) Only if he obtained prior permission to build.
C) Only if removing the building would not increase the rent.
D) Only if he pays a fine.

Key Takeaway
A building on waqf land is private property, but the owner may be forced to remove it if its presence denies the waqf a higher rent.

Monthly Lease on Waqf Land: Rescission and Building Protection
Second scenario: monthly lease on waqf land, third-party offer, and building protection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a monthly lease on waqf land can be rescinded at month-end upon a higher offer, and state when the lessee's building may remain despite rescission and when the trustee may purchase it.

Core Idea
A monthly lease renews each month; the trustee may rescind at month-end, but the lessee's building cannot be removed if it would harm the waqf.

This lesson covers the second scenario from al-Muhīṭ: a lessee builds on waqf land under a valid monthly lease. A third party offers higher rent. The trustee may rescind the lease at month-end because monthly leases renew each month. However, the building poses a problem: if removal would harm the waqf (e.g., structural damage), the lessee cannot be forced to demolish it. The trustee may purchase the building at market value (standing or dismantled, whichever is cheaper for the waqf) only if the lessee consents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the lease type
The lease is monthly (مشاهرة), which renews at the beginning of each month.
This allows rescission at month-end.
2
Determine rescission right
When a higher offer appears, the trustee may rescind the lease at the end of the current month.
The existing lease is not broken mid-month.
3
Assess building removal
If removing the building would harm the waqf (e.g., damage to foundation), the lessee is not compelled to remove it.
The building is private property, but harm to waqf prevents forced removal.
4
Evaluate purchase option
The trustee may offer to purchase the building at market value (either as is or dismantled) but only if the lessee agrees.
Forced purchase is impermissible without consent.
5
Conclude the outcome
If the lessee does not consent, the building remains, and the lessee continues to occupy, paying appropriate rent (likely market rent).
The passage ends with 'يبقى إلى أن...' implying further details.

Obligation of the Builder on Waqf Land to Pay Fair Rent
Ruling on the builder's obligation to pay fair rent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a builder on waqf land and identify the condition under which he may keep the building without raising the rent.

Core Idea
A builder on waqf must pay fair rent or remove; but if market rent is no higher, he stays at the current rent.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: someone builds on waqf land and pays a rent below the market rate. The Hanafi school balances the rights of the waqf beneficiaries with the hardship on the builder. The key is whether the builder can afford the fair rent without extreme loss.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is building on waqf land. The ruling is that the builder must either pay the fair market rent (ujrat al-mithl) or remove the building.
The default is that underpaying waqf rent is prohibited unless there is a valid excuse.
2
Find the exception
If the builder cannot find anyone willing to pay a higher rent (i.e., the market rate is the same as what he pays), he is not forced to remove the building and may stay at the current rent.
This exception is based on necessity (darura) – forcing removal would cause harm without any benefit to the waqf.
3
Apply the rule
The builder must assess the market rent. If it is higher, he must either increase his rent to match or remove his building. If it is not higher, he can continue at the same rent.
The burden is on the waqf administrator to prove that a higher rent is available.

Source Text

The owner of the building is required to remove the building and rent it from someone else because reduction from the fair rent is not permissible without necessity. If he cannot rent it for more than what he is currently paying, he is not required [to remove] and it is left in his hand at that rent because there is necessity. End. If you say: If he leased waqf land for years on multiple contracts for building and the contracts were ruled valid, then he built, and then someone else offered more, does the lease get rescinded? I say: It is stated in al-Muhit and others: If someone leased waqf land and built a shop on it and lived in it, and then someone else wanted to increase the rent and evict him from the shop, it is examined: if the rent was monthly, when the month ends, the administrator can rescind the lease because if the lease is monthly, it is renewed at the beginning of each month. Then it is examined: if removing the building does not harm the waqf, he may remove it because it is his property; if it does harm the waqf, he may not remove it because even though it is his property, he may not harm the waqf. Then if the tenant agrees that the administrator may take ownership of it for the waqf at its value whether built-up or removed, whichever is less harmful, the administrator may take ownership. If he does not agree, he may not take ownership because taking ownership without his consent is not permissible, so it remains until [...] people like it, it is an excessive increase, whether half or quarter, and it is what is not subject to the valuation of appraisers in the preferred view. Then he deliberated whether this is two narrations or whether the common people also intend by excessive fraud what was mentioned? None before us clarified it, and it was attributed to al-Dhakhirah like what is in al-Hawi. End. And what supports what is in al-Hawi is what the author presented a page earlier from al-Qunyah regarding a statement about excessive fraud being half of the equivalent and the like, for fraud is compared to increase, so half and the like were considered in it, similarly in increase. His statement: Then he examines: if removing the building etc. The scholar Qunli Zada said in his treatise after quoting something similar: In Fatawa Abi al-Layth: This is if the building was erected by the builder without the permission of the trustee; but if the building was by the order of the trustee, then the building belongs to the waqf, and the builder may reclaim from the trustee what he spent. End. He said: The apparent meaning is that he intended that the permission of the trustee for building is for the sake of the waqf; but if he granted permission for building for himself, and he built for himself and had witnesses to that, then the building does not belong to the waqf. His statement: And if he does not agree, he may not take ownership. Al-Ramli said: Similarly, if he agrees but the trustee does not agree, he is not forced because it is a transfer of ownership, and mutual consent is required. Then if the trustee does not agree, is the builder owed rent for his building? Apparently not, because it remained only for the benefit of the waqf, not for his benefit. Similarly, if the trustee agrees but the builder does not, because he cannot be forced to sell his property and leave the building on waqf land not for his benefit but for the benefit of the waqf by compulsion; and because if he were charged rent, he would suffer two harms: the harm of being forced to wait until the time of release and being charged rent, and no parallel is known in the law; and because if he is charged rent, he is forced to relinquish his property and release it from the waqf. This has been explicitly stated in al-Khulasa and others regarding a waqf shop with a building owned by another: if the owner of the building refuses to lease the plot at its equivalent rent, if the situation is such that if the building were removed, the plot could be rented [at a higher rate], he is required to remove the building; and if he rents it from someone else with the building, it is not permissible. So it is appropriate that the lease here is also not permissible unless he leases the plot with the building, and the owner of the building permits it, then it is permissible and the rent is divided between them. It is stated in al-Bazzaziyyah: If the building is owned and the plot is waqf, and the trustee leases with the permission of the owner of the building, the rent is divided between the building and the plot, and it is considered how much each would rent for, and what is attributable to the building belongs to the owner of the building. End. And similar is in the books. End. The speech of al-Ramli. I say: In Ijarat Manh al-Ghaffar, the building is taken over by the administrator for the waqf by force over the owner if the land would be damaged by removal; otherwise, his consent is necessary. Thus it is mentioned by the majority of commentators, including our master the author of al-Bahr. So one should rely on what is in the commentaries established for transmitting the madhhab, contrary to the statements of fatwas. And Allah knows best. End.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of rulings related to buildings erected on waqf land. It begins with a ruling: the owner of a building on waqf land must either pay the fair market rent or remove the building, because it is impermissible to rent at less than the market rate without necessity. However, if the market rate does not exceed what he is already paying, he is not forced to remove the structure, as that would cause undue hardship.

A key question arises: if someone leases waqf land for many years in multiple contracts, builds on it, and then another party offers a higher rent, does the original lease become invalid? The answer, sourced from al-Muhit, distinguishes based on the type of lease. If the lease is monthly (mushaharah), it renews each month, and at the end of each month the administrator (qayyim) may terminate the lease and lease to the higher bidder. If the lease is for a longer term, the lease remains binding unless there is an excessive increase in the market rent (ghabn fahish).

The passage then discusses the concept of ghabn fahish, defining it as an increase (or decrease) of about half or quarter of the market value, which is beyond normal fluctuations. There is a debate whether this refers to two separate narrations or a general understanding.

Further commentary from Qunli Zada clarifies that if the building was constructed with the trustee's permission specifically for the waqf, the building becomes waqf property and the builder can reclaim expenses from the trustee. If the trustee allowed building for the builder's own benefit with witnesses, the building remains the builder's property.

Al-Ramli's commentary addresses the situation where the builder refuses to sell the building to the waqf. In that case, the administrator cannot force the sale. However, the builder may be left with the building on waqf land, and he is not charged rent for the land because the building remains for the benefit of the waqf, not for his own benefit. The administrator cannot compel him to pay rent, as that would cause two harms: forcing him to wait and charging him rent, which has no parallel in Islamic law.

The passage concludes with a practical rule: if removing the building would damage the waqf, the administrator may take ownership of the building by force (with compensation) from the builder. Otherwise, the builder's consent is required. The preferred view is to rely on the established commentaries of the madhhab rather than individual fatwas.

Key Terms
أجر المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market rent for a property.
ضرورة (darura): Necessity that relaxes a normal prohibition or obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a builder on waqf land not required to remove his building?
A) When he built the building himself.
B) When he cannot find anyone willing to pay a higher rent.
C) When the waqf administrator agrees.
D) When the building is new.

Key Takeaway
A builder on waqf land must pay fair market rent or remove; but if no higher rent is available, he may stay at the current rent due to necessity.

Effect of Higher Rent Offers on Waqf Leases: Monthly vs Fixed Term
Ruling on higher rent offers and lease termination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when a higher rent offer can terminate a waqf lease and identify the threshold of ghabn fahish.

Core Idea
Monthly leases can be terminated for higher offers; longer leases require excessive rent increase (ghabn fahish) to dissolve.

A common dispute: a tenant builds on waqf land and later someone offers higher rent. Can the tenant be evicted? The Hanafi school answers by examining the lease type. Monthly leases (mushaharah) are treated as separate contracts each month, while longer leases are protected unless the rent difference is exorbitant (ghabn fahish).

Guided Path
1
Identify the lease type
Determine if the lease is monthly (mushaharah) or for a fixed term. The passage specifies that monthly leases renew each month.
The lease type is crucial for the ruling.
2
Apply the rule for monthly leases
For monthly leases, the administrator (qayyim) may rescind the lease at the end of each month and lease to someone offering a higher rent.
This is because the contract is renewed monthly.
3
Apply the rule for fixed-term leases
For longer-term leases, the lease remains binding unless the increase in market rent is excessive (ghabn fahish).
The passage defines ghabn fahish as an increase that is half or quarter of the market value, beyond normal fluctuation.
4
Define ghabn fahish
Ghabn fahish is an excessive disparity, here defined as half or quarter of the market rent. If the higher offer reaches this threshold, the lease may be terminated.
There is a discussion whether this threshold is fixed or depends on context; the preferred view is that half or quarter applies.

: (ثم ينظر إن كان رفع البناء الخ قال العلامة قنلي زاده في رسالته بعد نقله نحو ذلك وفي فتاوى أبي الليث : وهذا إذا كان البناء من الباني بغير إذن المتولي، فأما إن كان البناء بأمر المتولي كان البناء للوقف ويرجع الباني على المتولي بما أنفق اهـ . قال : والظاهر أنه أراد أن إذن المتولي بالبناء لأجل الوقف، أما إذا أذن بالبناء لنفسه فبنى لنفسه وأشهد عليه فلا يكون البناء للوقف . قوله : (وإن لم يرض لا يتملكه) قال الرملي : وكذلك لو رضي ولم يرض القيم لا يجبر لأنه تمليك وتملك فلا بد فيه من الرضا من الجانبين، ثم إن لم يرض القيم هل عليه أجرة لبنائه؟ الظاهر لا لأنه إنما بقي لمصلحة الوقف لا لمصلحته، وكذلك لو رضي البزازية : ولو كان البناء ملكاً والعرصة وقفاً وأجر المتولي بإذن مالك البناء فالأجر ينقسم على البناء والعرصة وينظر بكم يستأجر كل فما أصاب البناء فهو لمالك البناء اهـ. ومثله في الكتب. اهـ. كلام الرملي قلت وفي إجارات منح الغفار أن البناء يتملكه الناظر لجهة الوقف قهراً على صاحبه إذا كانت الأرض تنقص بالقلع وإلا فلا بد من رضاه؛ هكذا ذكره عامة الشارحون ممن صرح به مولانا صاحب البحر، فينبغي أن يعول على ما
