Rulings on the Waqf Administrator's Actions
Series of rulings on waqf administrator authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the waqf administrator's (qayyim) authority in six specific scenarios: entitlement to fees, rescission of sale and lease, mixing funds, discharge of rent, spending on legal documentation, and self-hiring.

Core Idea
The waqf administrator acts under strict fiduciary rules, but Hanafi law grants specific flexibilities for efficient management.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a series of rulings concerning the waqf administrator (qayyim or mutawalli). The text addresses disputes over fee entitlement, conditions for rescinding contracts, permissions for mixing funds, validity of discharging rent, spending on legal costs, and the prohibition against self-hiring. Understanding these rulings is essential for anyone managing a waqf or advising on endowment law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
For each statement, determine what action the administrator is taking and what the ruling (hukm) is: permissible, not permissible, valid, etc.
The text uses terms like 'yajuz' (it is permissible) and 'lam yajuz' (it is not permissible).
2
Note any conditions or limitations
Many rulings are conditional. For example, rescission of a sale is only allowed if the price was not above fair market value; mixing funds requires the judge's permission.
Pay attention to phrases like 'إذا لم يكن' (if it was not) and 'بإذن القاضي' (with the judge's permission).
3
Identify internal disagreements
Some rulings have disputes within the Hanafi school. For example, whether the administrator's fee goes to the dismissed or appointed person, and whether discharging the lessee is valid (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad vs. Abu Yusuf).
The text uses 'قيل' (it was said) to indicate a weaker opinion, and 'الأصح' (the most correct) to indicate the preferred view.
4
Determine the relied-upon view (mufta bihi)
For the fee issue, the preferred view is that it belongs to the appointed administrator. For the discharge issue, the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is presented as valid, though the text does not explicitly state the fatwa.
The fatwa on self-hiring is based on 'zahir al-riwaya' and is the operative ruling.
5
Connect the rulings to the principle of fiduciary duty
All rulings aim to protect the waqf's interests while allowing reasonable flexibility. The administrator is a trustee and must not act for personal gain (e.g., cannot hire himself).
The prohibition against mixing without permission ensures accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقيل أخذ الأجر للمعزول، والأصح أنه للمنصوب لأن المعزول أجرها للوقف لا لنفسه، ولو باع القيم داراً اشتراها بمال الوقف فله أن يقيل البيع مع المشتري إذا لم يكن البيع بأكثر من ثمن المثل، وكذا إذا عزل ونصب غيره فللمنصوب إقالته بلا خلاف. ولو أذن القاضي للقيم في خلط مال الوقف بماله تخفيفاً عليه جاز ولا يضمن وكذا القاضي إذا خلط مال الصغير بماله. وعن أبي يوسف : الوصي إذا خلط مال الصغير بماله لا يضمن وللقيم فسخ الإجارة مع المستأجر قبل قبض الأجر وينفذ فسخه على الوقف وبعد القبض لا. ولو أبرأ القيم المستأجر عن الأجرة بعد تمام المدة تصح البراءة عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد، ويضمن للقيم صرف شيء من مال الوقف إلى كتبة الفتوى ومحاضر الدعوى لاستخلاص الوقف، والمتولي إذا أجر نفسه في عمل المسجد وأخذ الأجرة لم يجز في ظاهر الرواية وبه يفتى اهـ.
So it was said: The fee (for administration) is taken by the dismissed administrator, but the correct view is that it is for the appointed one, because the dismissed one administered it for the waqf not for himself. If the administrator (qayyim) sold a house he bought with waqf funds, he may rescind the sale with the buyer as long as the sale was not for more than the fair price. Similarly, if he is dismissed and another appointed, the appointed one has the right to rescind without disagreement. If the judge permits the administrator to mix waqf funds with his own for ease, it is permissible and he is not liable. Likewise, the judge if he mixes the property of an orphan with his own. It is related from Abu Yusuf that if the executor (wasi) mixes the orphan's property with his own, he is not liable. The administrator may rescind a lease (ijara) with the lessee before receiving the rent, and his rescission is effective against the waqf, but after receipt he cannot. If the administrator discharges the lessee from the rent after the term ends, the discharge is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. It is permissible for the administrator to spend some of the waqf money on writers of fatwas and court records to recover the waqf. If the mutawalli hires himself for work in the mosque and takes wages, it is not permissible in the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya) and that is the fatwa. End.
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents several independent rulings concerning the authority of a waqf administrator (qayyim or mutawalli). The commentator states the positions without detailed proofs, typical of a commentary expanding on a matn. First, there is a dispute about who receives the administrative fee: the dismissed administrator or the newly appointed one? The correct view is that the appointed administrator gets it because the dismissed one acted for the waqf. Second, if the administrator sells a property bought with waqf funds, he may cancel the sale if the price was fair; if replaced, the new administrator also has that right. Third, mixing waqf funds with personal funds is allowed only with the judge's permission, and no liability attaches; this is similar for a judge mixing orphan's property. Fourth, the administrator may cancel a lease before receiving rent, but not after. Fifth, discharging a tenant from rent after the term is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (Abu Yusuf presumably disagrees). Sixth, spending waqf funds on legal documentation is permissible if it serves to recover the waqf. Finally, the administrator cannot hire himself for mosque work and take wages; this is based on the established transmission (zahir al-riwaya) and is the relied-upon fatwa. Each ruling reflects the Hanafi school's careful balancing of the administrator's fiduciary duty with practical necessity.

Key Terms
قيم (qayyim): The administrator of a waqf, appointed by the founder or judge, responsible for managing and preserving the endowment.
إقالة (iqalah): Mutual rescission of a sale contract by both parties.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The established and authoritative transmission of rulings from the early Hanafi masters, recorded in the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when may a waqf administrator (qayyim) rescind a sale of a house purchased with waqf funds?
A) At any time regardless of price.
B) Only if the sale price was not more than the fair market price (thaman al-mithl).
C) Only with the permission of the judge.
D) Only after collecting the entire price.

Key Takeaway
The waqf administrator's authority is carefully circumscribed by conditions ensuring protection of the endowment while allowing practical management.

Preferences Among Waqf Beneficiaries: Three Scenarios
Detailed rules on preference (tafdil) in waqf distribution based on countability of beneficiaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the three scenarios of beneficiary preference in waqf and apply the correct distribution method for each case.

Core Idea
In waqf, whether the mutawalli may prefer beneficiaries depends on whether they are countable — if uncountable, it's charity (flexible); if countable, it's a bequest (fixed).

The question of whether a mutawalli (administrator) can give preference to some beneficiaries over others arises frequently in waqf management. This lesson, drawn from al-Bazzaziyya and its commentaries, provides a clear classification based on the countability of the beneficiary groups. Understanding this distinction is essential for anyone administering a waqf or studying Hanafi distribution rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the beneficiary groups and their countability
Determine whether the beneficiaries are specified individuals or groups whose exact number is known (countable) or unknown/uncountable. Countability is the key factor.
If the founder's condition provides specific shares, that overrides the default categories.
2
Classify into one of three scenarios
Check if both groups are uncountable, both countable, or mixed. This determines the default distribution rule.
The text in al-Bazzaziyya lists these three faces (wujuh).
3
Apply the distribution rule
- Both uncountable: split revenue by group halves, then mutawalli may prefer individuals within each group. - Both countable: split by headcount, no preference allowed. - Mixed: split revenue by halves; countable group receives by head (no preference), uncountable group receives one share (preference allowed within that share).
The founder's express conditions may override the default rule.
4
Ensure consistency with founder's condition
Always check the waqf deed first. The founder's stipulation regarding preference (e.g., equal shares) must be followed; the default rule applies only in the absence of explicit condition.
The passage begins: 'التفضيل في القدر راجع إلى شرط الواقف'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If you say: May the mutawalli prefer some over others in amount and timing? I say: There is detail. Preference in amount reverts to the condition of the founder. He said in al-Bazzaziyya: If one endows a farm (day'ah) for the poor of his relatives or the poor of his village and makes its surplus for the needy, it is valid whether they are countable or not. If the administrator wishes to prefer some over others, the matter has aspects: If the endowment is for the poor of his relatives and his village, and they are countable or not countable, or one group is countable and the other not, then in the first aspect, the administrator may make half of the revenue for the poor relatives and half for the poor of the village, then give each, and prefer some over others as he wishes, because his intention is closeness (qurbah), and the same ruling applies in charity (sadaqah). In the second aspect, the revenue is distributed to the two groups according to their number, and he may not prefer some over others because his intention is a bequest (wasiyyah), and the same ruling applies in bequests. In the third aspect, the revenue is first divided between the two groups: it is given to those who are countable according to their number, and to those who are not countable one share, because those who can be counted have a bequest, and those who cannot be counted have a charity, and the recipient of charity is one (entity). Then this share is given to whomever of the non-countable the administrator wishes, and he may prefer some over others in this share. End. So his statement 'and spent his share for his own need' is incidental, not precautionary. Ponder. His statement: (they are countable or not countable) is in the copies and similarly in al-Bazzaziyya, but the correct is the opposite as in the third chapter of al-TatarKhaniyya where it said: they are not countable or countable. And thus the branch (tafri) becomes correct with his statement 'in the first aspect' and 'in the second aspect'; otherwise it does not. This is not hidden. For example, if the poor relatives are twenty and the poor of the village are ten, it is divided into thirty without preference, unlike the first aspect where it is divided into halves between the groups not by individuals because they are not countable. In the third aspect, the revenue is also divided into halves, then the half for those who are countable is divided by their number without preference, and the half for those who are not countable is given to whomever the administrator wishes, and by this what we have presented is clarified. Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage addresses the question of whether a mutawalli (administrator) may give preference to some beneficiaries over others in terms of amount (qadran) and timing (ta'jilan). The answer contains a detailed classification based on the nature of the waqf. The commentary cites al-Bazzaziyya, distinguishing three scenarios. First, if the waqf is for two groups (e.g., poor relatives and poor of the village) and both groups are uncountable (i.e., their exact number is unknown), the mutawalli may distribute half the revenue to each group and then within each group he may prefer individuals as he wishes, because the endowment is akin to charity (sadaqah) where the giver intends closeness to Allah and has discretion. Second, if both groups are countable (known numbers), the revenue must be divided according to their numbers, and no preference is allowed; this is because the endowment is treated like a bequest (wasiyyah) to specific individuals, where each has a fixed right. Third, if one group is countable and the other uncountable, the revenue is split between the two groups; the countable group receives according to their number (like a bequest), while the uncountable group receives a single share (like a charity), and within that share the administrator may prefer whoever he wishes. The passage also includes marginal notes from Ramli correcting a textual confusion and explaining the basis for the administrator's liability if he misappropriates funds. The commentator also notes that in the original al-Bazzaziyya, the wording about countable/uncountable is reversed in some copies, but the correct is as per al-TatarKhaniyya.

Key Terms
تفضيل (tafdil): Giving preference to some beneficiaries over others in the amount (qadr) or timing (ta'jil) of the waqf revenue.
صدقة (sadaqah): A charitable gift intended for closeness to Allah, where the giver has discretion over distribution.
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest or will, which specifies fixed shares for known individuals; here analogized to waqf for countable beneficiaries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bazzaziyya's classification, in which scenario may the mutawalli prefer some beneficiaries over others in amount as he wishes?
A) When both groups of beneficiaries are countable.
B) When both groups are uncountable.
C) When one group is countable and the other uncountable.
D) In all scenarios mentioned.

Key Takeaway
In waqf, the mutawalli's power to prefer beneficiaries depends on whether the beneficiary groups are countable (like a bequest, no preference) or uncountable (like charity, preference allowed).

Waqf — Endowment

Mutawalli's Authority to Prefer Beneficiaries in Waqf
Ruling with proof on mutawalli's preference in waqf distribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a mutawalli may prefer beneficiaries over others and classify a waqf as charity or bequest based on countability of beneficiaries.

Core Idea
Mutawalli may prefer when beneficiaries are not countable (charity); not when countable (bequest).

The authority of a waqf administrator (mutawalli) to give some beneficiaries more than others or pay them earlier is not absolute. It depends crucially on the nature of the waqf as intended by the founder. This lesson unpacks a detailed classification from al-Bazzaziyya that uses the countability of beneficiaries as the key factor, revealing the underlying logic of treating the waqf as either charity (ṣadaqa) or bequest (waṣiyya). We will trace how the ruling changes across three scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Question
Recognize that the passage addresses the question: can the mutawalli prefer some beneficiaries over others in amount (qadran) and timing (ta‘jīlan)? The answer requires a detailed classification.
The question is posed in the text as 'hal lil-mutawallī tafḍīl al-ba‘ḍ ʿalā al-ba‘ḍ qadran wa-ta‘jīlan?'
2
Classify the Waqf Based on Beneficiary Countability
Identify whether the beneficiaries are countable (yuḥṣawn) or not. Countable means a limited, enumerable set (e.g., 'my three children'); not countable means an indefinite or large group (e.g., 'the poor of the village'). This classification determines the legal nature of the waqf as a bequest or charity respectively.
The text initially had the clauses reversed; al-Tatarkhāniyya corrected the order: 'they are not countable or countable' – i.e., the first scenario assumes not countable, the second assumes countable.
3
Apply the Ruling for Pure Cases
In the first aspect (all beneficiaries not countable), the mutawalli may divide the yield into halves (if two groups) and then prefer individuals within each group at his discretion, because the waqf is treated as charity. In the second aspect (all countable), the yield must be divided by headcount without any preference, as it is a bequest.
The difference stems from the intention (qaṣd) of the founder: charity gives broad discretion; bequest requires strict adherence to shares.
4
Analyze the Mixed Case
When one group is countable and the other not, the yield is first split between the groups (e.g., half for each), then the countable group's share is divided by heads, while the uncountable group's share is given as a single share to whomever the mutawalli chooses, allowing preference within that group.
This hybrid treatment reflects the dual nature: those countable get a bequest (no preference), those uncountable get charity (preference allowed).
5
Evaluate the Ikhtilāf on Basis of Preference
The passage concludes that when preference is allowed, scholars differ on whether it should be based on need (ḥāja) or virtue (faḍīla). Both views are considered correct, giving the mutawalli flexibility.
This is a legitimate intra-Hanafi difference; the mufta bihi is to allow either basis.

Source Text

الثالث من التتارخانية حيث قال : وهم لا يحصون أو يحصون. وعلى هذا يصح التفريع بقوله ففي الوجه الأول وفي الوجه الثاني وإلا. فلا كما لا يخفى قوله : (تقسم الغلة إلى الفريقين بعددهم) أي تقسم على يصح الرؤوس فلو كان فقراء القرابة عشرين مثلاً وفقراء القرية عشرة تقسم على ثلاثين من غير تفضيل بخلاف الوجه الأول فإنها تقسم نصفين على الفريقين لا على الرؤوس لكونهم لا يحصون، وأما في الوجه الثالث فتقسم الغلة نصفين ،أيضاً ثم يقسم نصف من يحصون على عدد رؤوسهم بلا تفضيل ونصف من لا يحصون يعطى لمن شاء منهم وبه يتضح ما قدمناه قوله (كما قدمناه في مسألة الأوقاف المطلقة على الفقهاء للمتولي التفضيل، واختلفوا هل هو بالحاجة أو بالفضيلة وكل منهما صحيح.
Book of Waqf: The first year because that remained a right for all. So it appears that the mutawalli pays him from the yield of the second [year] whether they wish or not since he chose to follow them. Its implication is that if he did not disburse the share of the deprived person to himself but rather disbursed the yield to them and deprived one either due to absence at the time of division or out of obstinacy, then he shares with them and the mutawalli is not liable, and he pays him from the yield of the second from their shares. The apparent [meaning] in al-Hawi is that he follows them in what they took and does not give from the second more than his share, which is apparent because his right has become in their liability and the mutawalli has no authority to pay their debts. The requirement of principles is that the deprived person, in the case of disbursing all to them, has the option to hold the mutawalli liable for being transgressive, as well as to recourse against the beneficiaries. If you say: Does the mutawalli have the right to prefer some over others in amount and in advance? I say: There is detail; preference in amount reverts to the condition of the waqf founder. He said in al-Bazzaziyya: If one endows a farm upon the poor of his relatives or the poor of his village and makes its last [beneficiaries] the poor, it is permissible whether they are countable or not. And if the administrator intends to prefer some over others, the issue has aspects: If the waqf is upon the poor of his relatives and his village and they are countable or not countable, or one group is countable and the other not, then in the first aspect the administrator may put half the yield for the poor of the relatives and half for the poor of the village, then give each of them, and he may prefer some over others as he wishes because his intention is charity, and the ruling in charity is likewise. In the second aspect, the yield is disbursed to the groups according to their number, and he may not prefer some over others because his intention is a bequest, and the ruling in a bequest is likewise. In the third aspect, the yield is first divided between the groups, then disbursed to those who are countable according to their number, and to those who are not countable one share because those who are countable have a bequest, and those who are not have charity, and the recipient of charity is one. Then this share is given to whomever he wishes among those who are not countable, and he may prefer some over others in this share. And we have presented that a group... thus the mutawalli pays him from the yield of the second. Al-Ramli said: If he meant from their shares, then he explicitly stated that he has the right to take and they all recourse against the administrator, so what is the meaning of this speech? And if he meant from other than their shares, the apparent contradicts this apparent. There is no apparent contradiction between the two statements, i.e., the statement of al-Hawi and the statement of al-Khaniyya. Consider his statement: (And he does not hold the mutawalli liable); al-Ramli said: The apparent is that he may hold him liable because he had no right to divert his entitlement to them, so he was transgressive and is liable. So his statement 'and disbursed his share to his own need' is incidental, not restrictive. Consider his statement: (And they are countable or not countable) in the copies, and it is likewise in al-Bazzaziyya, but the correct is the opposite as in the third chapter of al-Tatarkhaniyya where it says: and they are not countable or countable. Upon this the subdivision is correct with his statement: in the first aspect and in the second aspect; otherwise not, as is not hidden. His statement: (The yield is divided to the groups according to their number) means it is divided according to heads. So if the poor of the relatives are twenty and the poor of the village are ten, it is divided into thirty without preference, unlike the first aspect where it is divided into halves among the groups not according to heads because they are not countable. As for the third aspect, the yield is divided into halves, then the half of those countable is divided according to their heads without preference, and the half of those not countable is given to whomever is wished among them, and thereby what we have presented is clarified. His statement: (As we have presented in the issue of absolute endowments for the fuqaha', the mutawalli has preference, and they differed whether it is by need or by virtue, and both are correct.)
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (with proof) regarding the authority of the mutawalli (administrator of a waqf) to prefer some beneficiaries over others both in the amount they receive and in the timing of payment. The author begins by discussing the case of a deprived beneficiary who was not present at distribution. The mutawalli must compensate him from future yields, but the ruling on whether the mutawalli is liable for the deprived beneficiary's right is nuanced: if the mutawalli distributed the entire yield to the others, the deprived person may hold the mutawalli liable for the transgression or may recourse directly against the beneficiaries. Then the core question is posed: can the mutawalli deliberately prefer some beneficiaries over others, in amount and in advance payment? The answer provides a detailed classification based on the intention of the waqf founder. If the beneficiaries are not countable (e.g., a large indefinite group), the disbursement is considered charity (ṣadaqa), and the mutawalli may prefer as he wishes. If they are countable (e.g., a limited list of individuals), the disbursement is akin to a bequest (waṣiyya), and preference is not allowed. A mixed case is also addressed. The text then includes critical notes from al-Ramlī correcting some textual points and clarifying the proper interpretation of the conditions. The comment on the phrase 'they are countable or not countable' shows a correction from the Tatarkhāniyya reversing the order of the clauses. Finally, the author confirms that the mutawalli has discretion in preference, with a difference of opinion on whether the basis is need or virtue, both being valid.

Key Terms
التفضيل (al-tafḍīl): The act of preferring some beneficiaries over others in amount or timing of distribution.
المتولي (al-mutawallī): The administrator or custodian of a waqf, responsible for distributing its revenues.
يحصون (yuḥṣawn): Being countable or enumerable as a limited set of beneficiaries.
المحروم (al-maḥrūm): A beneficiary who was deprived of his share due to absence or other reasons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which case may the mutawalli prefer some beneficiaries over others in the amount given?
A) When the beneficiaries are countable and the waqf is like a bequest.
B) When the beneficiaries are not countable and the waqf is like a charity.
C) In all cases, without condition.
D) Only when the waqf founder explicitly allows it.

Key Takeaway
The mutawalli's authority to prefer beneficiaries depends on countability: not countable (charity) → preference allowed; countable (bequest) → no preference.

Advance Payment of Waqf Revenues (Ta'jil)
Derivation of a ruling on advance payment by analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on advance payment of waqf revenues and derive its permissibility by analogy.

Core Idea
Advance payment of waqf revenues is permissible by analogy with early payment of salaries, but caution is advised.

The author of Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a question: can the custodian of a waqf advance revenues to some beneficiaries before the due time? Finding no explicit text, he uses qiyas to permit it, drawing on rulings about early payment of salaries. He then counters an objection that waqf funds are more restricted than public funds, analogizing to a shared debt. This lesson walks through this legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and absence of explicit text
The author admits there is no clear transmission (naql) on advance payment to some beneficiaries. This sets the stage for ijtihad by inference.
2
Locate the analogous case from al-Bazzaziyya
The author cites the permissibility of a collector taking his fee before due date and a judge receiving salary early. He argues the same principle applies to waqf.
This is qiyas with the illa being need and benefit.
3
Understand the objection against the analogy
The objection: waqf wealth is specific to beneficiaries, unlike public treasury. Therefore advancing funds to one may prejudice others.
4
Analyze the author's response using the shared-debt analogy
The author compares beneficiaries to co-creditors in a joint debt. Paying one creditor is valid; the absent co-creditor has a choice. Similarly, beneficiaries may be given a choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما التعجيل للبعض فلم أر فيه نقلاً صريحاً، وينبغي أن يجوز استنباطاً مما في البزازية : المصدق إذا أخذ عمالته قبل الوجوب أو القاضي استوفى رزقه قبل المدة جاز، والأفضل عدم التعجيل لاحتمال أن لا يعيش إلى المدة .اهـ. فإن قيل: لا يقاس عليه لأن مال الوقف حق المستحقين على الخصوص فليس له أن يخصص أحداً، ومال بيت المال حق العامة . قلت : غايته أن يكون كدين مشترك بين اثنين وجب لهما بسبب واحد، والدائن إذا دفع لأحدهما نصيبه جاز له ذلك غايته أن الشريك الغائب إذا حضر خير إن شاء اتبع شريكه وشاركه، وإن شاء أخذ من المديون فكذلك يمكن أن يقال : يخير المستحق كذلك كما في مسألة المحروم. ثم رأيت في القنية : لم يكن في المسجد إمام ولا مؤذن واجتمعت غلات الإمامة والتأذين سنين ثم نصب إمام ومؤذن لا يجوز صرف شيء من تلك الغلات إليهما. وقال برهان الدين صاحب المحيط : لو عجلوه للمستقبل كان حسناً إلى آخر ما ذكره . وفي البزازية : المتولي لو أمياً فاستأجر الكاتب لحسابه لا يجوز له إعطاء الأجرة من مال الوقف، ولو استأجر لكنس المسجد وفتحه وإغلاقه بمال المسجد يجوز اهـ. وليس لأحد الناظرين التصرف دون الآخر عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف. وفي الخانية: ولو أن قيمين في وقف أقام كل قيم قاضي بلدة غير قاضي بلدة أخرى هل يجوز لكل واحد منهما أن يتصرف بدون الآخر؟ قال الشيخ الإمام إسماعيل الزاهد ينبغي أن يجوز تصرف كل واحد منهما، ولو أن واحداً من هذين القاضيين أراد أن يعزل القيم الذي أقامه القاضي الآخر فإن رأى القاضي المصلحة في عزل الآخر كان له ذلك وإلا فلا .اهـ وفيه دليل على أن للقاضي عزل منصوب قاض آخر بغير خيانة إذا رأى المصلحة .اهـ. فإن قلت: هل لأحد الناظرين أن يؤجر الآخر؟ قلت: لا يجوز لما في الخانية من كتاب الوصايا : لو باع أحد الوصيين لصاحبه شيئاً من التركة لا يجوز عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد لأن عندهما لا ينفرد أحد الوصيين بالتصرف والناظر إما وصي أو كيل. وفي جامع الفصولين: ليس للوصي في هذا الزمان أخذ مال اليتيم مضاربة ولا للقيم أن يزرع في أرض الوقف .اهـ. فإذا ثبت عند القاضي أنه زرع ينبغي أن يكون خيانة يستحق بها العزل وفي جامع الفصولين ولو أذن قيم مؤذناً ليخدم مسجداً وقطع له الأجر وجعل ذلك أجرة المنزل وهو أجر المثل جاز. وفي الخانية : المتولي إذا مسألة المحروم أن يتبعهم المحروم) قال الرملي: قدم في أن يتبع المتولي فيضمنه وبين أنه يخير بين لكنه خص ذلك بما إذا حرمه وصرف ذلك لنفسه لا مطلقاً أنه خلاف الفقه لأن حاصله أنه دفع مال الغير بلا إذن الغير والدافع متعد بالدفع والآخذ بالأخذ فكان له أن يضمن من شاء منهما
As for advance payment to some, I have not found an explicit transmission regarding it, and it should be permissible by derivation from what is in al-Bazzaziyya: The collector, if he takes his fee before its obligation, or the judge receives his salary before the term, it is permissible, and it is better not to advance due to the possibility that he may not survive until the term. So if it is said: It is not analogous because waqf wealth is the right of the beneficiaries specifically, so he may not allocate to one, while Bayt al-Mal wealth is the right of the general public. I say: At most, it is like a shared debt owed to two due to one cause. If the creditor pays one of them his share, it is permissible for him to do so; at most, the absent partner, when he arrives, is given the choice: if he wishes, he follows his partner and shares, and if he wishes, he takes from the debtor. Likewise, it can be said: The beneficiary is given the choice similarly, as in the case of the deprived one. Then I saw in al-Qunyah: If there was no imam or mu'adhdhin in the mosque and the revenues of the imamate and adhan accumulated for years, then an imam and mu'adhdhin are appointed, it is not permissible to disburse any of those revenues to them. Burhan al-Din, the author of al-Muhit, said: If they advanced it for the future, it is good, to the end of what he mentioned. In al-Bazzaziyya: If the mutawalli is illiterate and hires a scribe for his account, it is not permissible for him to give the wage from waqf funds; but if he hires someone to sweep the mosque and open and close it, it is permissible. And neither of the two custodians may act without the other according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], contrary to Abu Yusuf's earlier view. In al-Khaniyya: If there are two custodians in a waqf, each appointed by a different qadi of a different town, is it permissible for each to act without the other? Shaykh al-Imam Ismail al-Zahid said: The action of each should be permissible. And if one of these two judges wishes to dismiss the custodian appointed by the other, if the judge sees benefit in dismissing the other, he may do so; otherwise not. This contains evidence that a judge may dismiss the appointee of another judge without treachery if he sees benefit. If you say: May one of the custodians lease to the other? I say: It is not permissible, because in al-Khaniyya from the book of wills: If one of the executors sells something from the estate to his fellow, it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because in their view neither executor may act alone. The custodian is either an executor or an agent. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: It is not for the executor in this time to take the orphan's wealth in mudarabah, nor for the qayyim to cultivate waqf land. So if it is established before the qadi that he cultivated, it should be treachery deserving dismissal. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: If a qayyim authorizes a mu'adhdhin to serve a mosque and fixes his wage and makes it a rental for the house, and it is the equivalent wage, it is permissible. In al-Khaniyya: The mutawalli, if the case of the deprived one, that he follows them... Al-Ramli said: He presented that he follows the mutawalli and holds him liable, and explained that he has a choice, but he specified that to be when he deprived him and disbursed that to himself, not absolutely, that it is contrary to fiqh because the result is that he paid another's wealth without the other's permission; the payer is transgressive in paying and the taker in taking; so he may hold liable whichever he wishes of them.
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage contains several independent rulings related to waqf administration. First, the issue of advance payment (ta'jīl) to some beneficiaries: the author finds no explicit text but derives permissibility by analogy from the case of a collector taking his fee early or a judge receiving salary before term. An objection is raised that waqf funds are specific to beneficiaries, unlike public treasury funds. The author responds by analogizing to a shared debt, where paying one creditor in advance is valid, and the absent partner has a choice. Then, a ruling from al-Qunyah: accumulated revenues from a mosque's imam and mu'adhdhin positions cannot be paid to newly appointed ones unless advanced for the future. Next, a ruling from al-Bazzaziyya: an illiterate mutawalli cannot pay a scribe from waqf funds for his own account, but hiring for cleaning and opening/closing the mosque is permissible. Then, a dispute on dual custodians: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, one custodian cannot act without the other, but Abu Yusuf had a differing earlier view. The Khaniyya cites a case where each custodian is appointed by a different qadi; Ismail al-Zahid allows independent action. The passage also discusses whether one custodian can lease to the other: not permissible. Then, rulings on the qayyim not engaging in mudarabah with orphan's wealth or cultivating waqf land. Finally, the case of the deprived beneficiary returns: the mutawalli may be held liable if he disbursed to others, but the choice of the deprived person is clarified based on al-Ramli's commentary.

Key Terms
التعجيل (al-ta'jīl): Advance payment of waqf revenues to beneficiaries before the due time.
المحروم (al-maḥrūm): A beneficiary who was deprived of their share; the case of the deprived one is referenced for the choice given to beneficiaries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on advancing waqf revenues to some beneficiaries?
A) Absolutely prohibited
B) Permissible but better not to
C) Permissible only with the qadi's permission
D) Permissible only for imam and mu'adhdhin

Key Takeaway
Advance payment of waqf revenues is permissible by analogy, but caution is the recommended practice.

Hiring for Waqf Services and Prohibited Transactions for Custodians
Rulings on permissible and impermissible uses of waqf funds for hiring and personal transactions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible and impermissible uses of waqf funds for hiring and personal transactions.

Core Idea
Waqf funds cannot be used for the custodian's personal benefit, but services directly benefiting the waqf may be hired.

This lesson covers two specific prohibitions and one permission in waqf administration. First, an illiterate mutawalli cannot pay a scribe from waqf funds for his own accounting; but hiring workers for mosque maintenance is allowed. Second, an executor (wasi) or qayyim cannot engage in mudarabah with orphan's wealth or cultivate waqf land. These rulings protect waqf and orphan assets from misuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the illiterate mutawalli scenario
If the mutawalli himself is illiterate and needs a scribe to write accounts, he cannot pay the scribe from waqf funds because the benefit is personal.
2
Contrast the permissible hiring
Hiring someone to sweep the mosque and open/close it is a direct benefit to the waqf, so using waqf funds is permissible.
3
Examine the prohibition on mudarabah and cultivation
An executor (wasi) cannot take orphan's wealth in mudarabah (partnership) because it risks loss; similarly, a qayyim cannot cultivate waqf land for personal gain.
4
Determine the consequence of violation
If a qayyim does cultivate, it is considered treachery and grounds for dismissal by the qadi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما التعجيل للبعض فلم أر فيه نقلاً صريحاً، وينبغي أن يجوز استنباطاً مما في البزازية : المصدق إذا أخذ عمالته قبل الوجوب أو القاضي استوفى رزقه قبل المدة جاز، والأفضل عدم التعجيل لاحتمال أن لا يعيش إلى المدة .اهـ. فإن قيل: لا يقاس عليه لأن مال الوقف حق المستحقين على الخصوص فليس له أن يخصص أحداً، ومال بيت المال حق العامة . قلت : غايته أن يكون كدين مشترك بين اثنين وجب لهما بسبب واحد، والدائن إذا دفع لأبي يوسف. وفي الخانية: ولو أن قيمين في وقف أقام كل قيم قاضي بلدة غير قاضي بلدة أخرى هل يجوز لكل واحد منهما أن يتصرف بدون الآخر؟ قال الشيخ الإمام إسماعيل الزاهد ينبغي أن يجوز تصرف كل واحد منهما، ولو .اهـ. فإن قلت: هل لأحد الناظرين أن يؤجر الآخر؟ قلت: لا يجوز لما في الخانية من كتاب الوصايا : لو باع أحد الوصيين لصاحبه شيئاً من التركة لا يجوز عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد لأن عندهما لا ينفرد أحد الوصيين بالتصرف والناظر إما وصي أو كيل. وفي جامع الفصولين: ليس للوصي في هذا الزمان أخذ مال اليتيم مضاربة ولا للقيم أن يزرع في أرض الوقف .اهـ. فإذا ثبت عند القاضي أنه زرع ينبغي أن يكون خيانة يستحق بها العزل وفي جامع الفصولين ولو أذن قيم مؤذناً ليخدم مسجداً وقطع له الأجر وجعل ذلك أجرة المنزل وهو أجر المثل جاز. وفي الخانية : المتولي إذا مسألة المحروم أن يتبعهم المحروم) قال الرملي: قدم في أن يتبع المتولي فيضمنه وبين أنه يخير بين لكنه خص ذلك بما إذا حرمه وصرف ذلك لنفسه لا مطلقاً أنه خلاف الفقه لأن حاصله أنه دفع مال الغير بلا إذن الغير والدافع متعد بالدفع والآخذ بالأخذ فكان له أن يضمن من شاء منهما
As for advance payment to some, I have not found an explicit transmission regarding it, and it should be permissible by derivation from what is in al-Bazzaziyya: The collector, if he takes his fee before its obligation, or the judge receives his salary before the term, it is permissible, and it is better not to advance due to the possibility that he may not survive until the term. So if it is said: It is not analogous because waqf wealth is the right of the beneficiaries specifically, so he may not allocate to one, while Bayt al-Mal wealth is the right of the general public. I say: At most, it is like a shared debt owed to two due to one cause. If the creditor pays one of them his share, it is permissible for him to do so; at most, the absent partner, when he arrives, is given the choice: if he wishes, he follows his partner and shares, and if he wishes, he takes from the debtor. Likewise, it can be said: The beneficiary is given the choice similarly, as in the case of the deprived one. Then I saw in al-Qunyah: If there was no imam or mu'adhdhin in the mosque and the revenues of the imamate and adhan accumulated for years, then an imam and mu'adhdhin are appointed, it is not permissible to disburse any of those revenues to them. Burhan al-Din, the author of al-Muhit, said: If they advanced it for the future, it is good, to the end of what he mentioned. In al-Bazzaziyya: If the mutawalli is illiterate and hires a scribe for his account, it is not permissible for him to give the wage from waqf funds; but if he hires someone to sweep the mosque and open and close it, it is permissible. And neither of the two custodians may act without the other according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], contrary to Abu Yusuf's earlier view. In al-Khaniyya: If there are two custodians in a waqf, each appointed by a different qadi of a different town, is it permissible for each to act without the other? Shaykh al-Imam Ismail al-Zahid said: The action of each should be permissible. And if one of these two judges wishes to dismiss the custodian appointed by the other, if the judge sees benefit in dismissing the other, he may do so; otherwise not. This contains evidence that a judge may dismiss the appointee of another judge without treachery if he sees benefit. If you say: May one of the custodians lease to the other? I say: It is not permissible, because in al-Khaniyya from the book of wills: If one of the executors sells something from the estate to his fellow, it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because in their view neither executor may act alone. The custodian is either an executor or an agent. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: It is not for the executor in this time to take the orphan's wealth in mudarabah, nor for the qayyim to cultivate waqf land. So if it is established before the qadi that he cultivated, it should be treachery deserving dismissal. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: If a qayyim authorizes a mu'adhdhin to serve a mosque and fixes his wage and makes it a rental for the house, and it is the equivalent wage, it is permissible. In al-Khaniyya: The mutawalli, if the case of the deprived one, that he follows them... Al-Ramli said: He presented that he follows the mutawalli and holds him liable, and explained that he has a choice, but he specified that to be when he deprived him and disbursed that to himself, not absolutely, that it is contrary to fiqh because the result is that he paid another's wealth without the other's permission; the payer is transgressive in paying and the taker in taking; so he may hold liable whichever he wishes of them.
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage contains several independent rulings related to waqf administration. First, the issue of advance payment (ta'jīl) to some beneficiaries: the author finds no explicit text but derives permissibility by analogy from the case of a collector taking his fee early or a judge receiving salary before term. An objection is raised that waqf funds are specific to beneficiaries, unlike public treasury funds. The author responds by analogizing to a shared debt, where paying one creditor in advance is valid, and the absent partner has a choice. Then, a ruling from al-Qunyah: accumulated revenues from a mosque's imam and mu'adhdhin positions cannot be paid to newly appointed ones unless advanced for the future. Next, a ruling from al-Bazzaziyya: an illiterate mutawalli cannot pay a scribe from waqf funds for his own account, but hiring for cleaning and opening/closing the mosque is permissible. Then, a dispute on dual custodians: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, one custodian cannot act without the other, but Abu Yusuf had a differing earlier view. The Khaniyya cites a case where each custodian is appointed by a different qadi; Ismail al-Zahid allows independent action. The passage also discusses whether one custodian can lease to the other: not permissible. Then, rulings on the qayyim not engaging in mudarabah with orphan's wealth or cultivating waqf land. Finally, the case of the deprived beneficiary returns: the mutawalli may be held liable if he disbursed to others, but the choice of the deprived person is clarified based on al-Ramli's commentary.

Key Terms
المتولي (al-mutawallī): The administrator of a waqf; also called nāẓir or qayyim.
المضاربة (al-muḍārabah): A profit-sharing partnership; forbidden for executors with orphan's wealth in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a mutawalli hires a scribe to write reports for his own accounting?
A) Permissible because it is necessary
B) Permissible only with qadi's consent
C) Not permissible because the benefit is personal
D) Not permissible only if mutawalli is rich

Key Takeaway
Waqf funds may only be used for services that directly benefit the waqf, not for the custodian's personal needs.

Authority of Dual Custodians (Naziran) in Waqf Administration
Ruling on the authority of dual custodians and related transactions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi rule on dual custodians and identify the exception when they are appointed by different qadis.

Core Idea
Two custodians of a waqf cannot act independently unless each is appointed by a different qadi, in which case independent action is permissible.

When a waqf has two custodians (naziran or qayyiman), can one act without the other? The Hanafi school's majority view is no, based on the analogy with executors. However, an exception arises when each custodian is appointed by a different qadi, as stated by Ismail al-Zahid. This lesson explores the rule, the exception, and the related ruling on leasing between custodians.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions), neither custodian may act alone. Abu Yusuf had a differing earlier view, but the relied-upon position is joint authority.
2
Examine the exception for different qadis
In al-Khaniyya, if each custodian is appointed by a different qadi, Ismail al-Zahid permits each to act independently. This is based on practical necessity.
3
Understand the implication for dismissal
The text also indicates that a qadi may dismiss a custodian appointed by another qadi if he sees public benefit, even without proven treachery.
4
Apply the rule to leasing between custodians
Can one custodian lease property to the other? The answer is no, by analogy with executors selling to each other. This is because neither has independent authority to transact with the other.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

المدة .اهـ. فإن قيل: لا يقاس عليه لأن مال الوقف حق المستحقين على الخصوص فليس له أن يخصص أحداً، ومال بيت المال حق العامة . قلت : غايته أن يكون كدين مشترك بين اثنين وجب لهما بسبب واحد، والدائن إذا دفع .اهـ. فإن قلت: هل لأحد الناظرين أن يؤجر الآخر؟ قلت: لا يجوز لما في الخانية من كتاب الوصايا : لو باع أحد الوصيين لصاحبه شيئاً من التركة لا يجوز عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد لأن عندهما لا ينفرد أحد الوصيين As for advance payment to some, I have not found an explicit transmission regarding it, and it should be permissible by derivation from what is in al-Bazzaziyya: The collector, if he takes his fee before its obligation, or the judge receives his salary before the term, it is permissible, and it is better not to advance due to the possibility that he may not survive until the term. Mutawalli's Discretion in Absolute Waqf Distribution
Ruling on mutawalli's preference in absolute waqf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the mutawalli's discretion in distributing absolute endowments and explain the valid bases for preference.

Core Idea
A mutawalli may prefer some jurists over others based on need or merit—both are legally valid.

Absolute endowments are those where beneficiaries are described as a general class, e.g., 'for the fuqaha'. The mutawalli (custodian) must distribute the revenues, but may he favor some over others? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that preference is allowed and can be based on either need or merit. Let's unpack the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of waqf
Recognize that 'absolute endowments' means the beneficiaries are not named individually but belong to a general category (here, jurists).
2
State the ruling on the mutawalli's power
The author states that the mutawalli has the right to prefer some beneficiaries over others (al-tafḍīl).
3
Identify the two bases for preference
The scholars differed: one view says preference is based on need (al-ḥājah), another says it is based on merit (al-faḍīlah).
4
Confirm the legal validity
The text concludes 'wa kullun minhumā ṣaḥīḥ' (both are correct), so the mutawalli may choose either criterion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قدمناه الأوقاف المطلقة على الفقهاء للمتولي التفضيل، واختلفوا هل هو بالحاجة أو بالفضيلة وكل منهما صحيح.
We have presented that absolute endowments (given) to jurists: the mutawalli has preference (in distribution). They disagreed whether it is by need or by merit, and both are correct.
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling about absolute endowments (waqf mawquf 'ala al-fuqaha') where the beneficiaries are unspecified jurists. The mutawalli (custodian) has the discretion to distribute the revenues preferentially among them. Scholars differed on the basis for preference: some say it should be based on need (al-hajah), others on merit (al-fadilah). The author states that both methods are valid (sahih), meaning the mutawalli may choose either criterion. This is a general principle of waqf administration.

Key Terms
الأوقاف المطلقة (al-awqāf al-muṭlaqah): Endowments where the beneficiaries are not specified individually, e.g., 'for the fuqaha' (jurists)' as a general class.
التفضيل (al-tafḍīl): The act of preferring some beneficiaries over others in allocation of waqf revenues.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must distribute equally among all.
B) He may distribute based on need or merit; both are valid.
C) He must prefer the most needy.
D) He must prefer the most meritorious.

Key Takeaway
In absolute endowments, the mutawalli may prefer some beneficiaries over others based on need or merit, without being required to equalize.

Advancing Waqf Revenues and the Case of the Mahrum
Ruling on advancing waqf revenues to a specific beneficiary before the term.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on advancing waqf revenues to a specific beneficiary before the term and explain the analogy to joint debt.

Core Idea
Advancing waqf revenues to one beneficiary is permissible by analogy to paying one joint debtor, but the deprived beneficiary can seek recourse.

This passage addresses a practical question: can a mutawalli pay early to one beneficiary before the scheduled distribution? The author finds no explicit text but uses qiyas (analogy) from the permissibility of early payment to a zakat collector or judge. He then defends this against an objection and extends the analogy to the case of the mahrum (deprived beneficiary).

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the ruling sought? The author wants to determine whether a mutawalli may advance waqf revenues to one specific beneficiary before the term.
The ruling is not found explicitly in earlier texts, so analogy is used.
2
Examine the asl (original case)
The author finds an analogous case in al-Bazzaziyya: a zakat collector may take his fee before zakat is due, and a judge may receive salary before the term. This is the basis of the analogy.
The asl involves permissibility of early payment to a specific person.
3
Analyze the objection
One might object that waqf revenues are the specific right of named beneficiaries, unlike bayt al-mal which belongs to the general public. Thus, singling out one is problematic.
The objection challenges the suitability of the analogy.
4
Follow the Hanafi rebuttal
The author responds that waqf revenues are like a joint debt owed to multiple creditors. Paying one creditor his share is permissible; the absentee creditor later has a choice to pursue the paid partner or the debtor. Similarly, the deprived beneficiary can choose whom to hold liable.
This rebuttal establishes the analogy and addresses the objection.
5
Extend to the mahrum case
The author cites al-Ramli to clarify the mahrum: if the mutawalli wrongfully paid one beneficiary (especially for personal gain), the deprived beneficiary may sue either the mutawalli or the recipient.
The mahrum case shows the practical application of the analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما التعجيل للبعض فلم أر فيه نقلاً صريحاً، وينبغي أن يجوز استنباطاً مما في البزازية : المصدق إذا أخذ عمالته قبل الوجوب أو القاضي استوفى رزقه قبل المدة جاز، والأفضل عدم التعجيل لاحتمال أن لا يعيش إلى المدة .اهـ. فإن قيل: لا يقاس عليه لأن مال الوقف حق المستحقين على الخصوص فليس له أن يخصص أحداً، ومال بيت المال حق العامة . قلت : غايته أن يكون كدين مشترك بين اثنين وجب لهما بسبب واحد، والدائن إذا دفع لأحدهما نصيبه جاز له ذلك غايته أن الشريك الغائب إذا حضر خير إن شاء اتبع شريكه وشاركه، وإن شاء أخذ من المديون فكذلك يمكن أن يقال : يخير المستحق كذلك كما في مسألة المحروم. مسألة المحروم: قال الرملي: قدم في أن يتبع المتولي فيضمنه وبين أنه يخير بين لكنه خص ذلك بما إذا حرمه وصرف ذلك لنفسه لا مطلقاً أنه خلاف الفقه لأن حاصله أنه دفع مال الغير بلا إذن الغير والدافع متعد بالدفع والآخذ بالأخذ فكان له أن يضمن من شاء منهما
As for advancing (payment) to some (beneficiaries), I have not seen a clear transmission about it. It should be permissible analogically from what is in al-Bazzaziyya: 'The zakat collector if he takes his fee before the obligation, or the judge if he receives his salary before the term, it is permissible. Better not to advance due to the possibility that he may not live until the term.' End. If it is said: It cannot be analogized because waqf property is the right of the beneficiaries specifically, so he may not single out one, while bayt al-mal property is the right of the general public. I (the author) say: The utmost (of this) is that it is like a joint debt owed to two persons due to one cause, and if the creditor pays one of them his share, that is permissible for him. The utmost is that the absent partner, when he appears, has the choice: if he wishes he may pursue his partner and participate with him, and if he wishes he may take from the debtor. Similarly, it can be said: the beneficiary (in waqf) has the choice as well, as in the case of the mahrum. The case of the mahrum: al-Ramli said: He advanced that the beneficiary may follow the mutawalli and make him liable, and he explained that he has the choice between [؟], but he restricted that to when (the mutawalli) deprived him and spent it on himself, not absolutely, because that is contrary to fiqh since the sum of it is that he paid another's property without permission of the owner, the payer is a transgressor in paying and the receiver in taking, so he (the deprived beneficiary) may make liable whomever he wishes of the two.
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific ruling: may the mutawalli advance waqf revenues to a particular beneficiary before the scheduled time? The author states he found no explicit text, but analogizes from the permissibility of a zakat collector taking his fee early or a judge taking salary early, as recorded in al-Bazzaziyya. However, an objection is raised: waqf property is the specific right of identified beneficiaries, so favoring one is problematic, unlike bayt al-mal (public treasury) which belongs to all. The author responds by likening it to a joint debt owed to two persons from one cause: the creditor may pay one his share, and the absent partner later has the option to either seek reimbursement from the paid partner or from the debtor. Similarly, in waqf, the deprived beneficiary (mahrum) may choose to hold the mutawalli liable or the recipient beneficiary? Al-Ramli's commentary clarifies the mahrum case: the deprived beneficiary may pursue the mutawalli (who wrongfully paid) or the recipient, but only if the mutawalli acted for his own benefit, not if he acted in good faith. The ruling is based on the principle that paying another's property without permission is transgression.

Key Terms
مسألة المحروم (mas’alat al-mahrūm): The case of a beneficiary who is deprived of his share of waqf due to the mutawalli wrongfully paying another. The deprived one has the right to seek compensation.
تجوز (yajūz): Permissible, but not obligatory. The author uses it to indicate the ruling derived by analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the author's ruling on advancing waqf revenues to a specific beneficiary before the term?
A) Forbidden because it is not explicitly mentioned.
B) Permissible by analogy (istinbat) from the case of zakat collector and judge.
C) Permissible only if all beneficiaries consent.
D) Obligatory if the beneficiary is needy.

Key Takeaway
Advancing waqf revenues to a specific beneficiary is permissible by analogy to joint debt, but the deprived beneficiary has a right of recourse against the mutawalli or the recipient.

Co-Nazhir Authority and the Exception of Independent Action
Intra-Hanafi dispute on co-nazhir autonomy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default Hanafi rule on co-nazhir authority, identify the exceptional fatwa allowing independent action when appointed by different judges, and apply the prohibition on one nazhir hiring the other.

Core Idea
Co-nazhirs must act jointly by default, but necessity permits independent action when appointed by different judges.

This lesson addresses the authority of two co-nazhirs (overseers) of a waqf. The Hanafi school has a default rule that they must act jointly, but a later fatwa relaxes this for practical administration. We will also examine a specific case: can one nazhir hire the other? The answer is no, analogous to co-executors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule
Read the first sentence: 'And it is not permissible for one of the two overseers to act without the other according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).' This is the default rule: joint action is required.
The two are Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Note the dissent within the school
The text says 'contrary to Abu Yusuf.' Abu Yusuf disagreed, permitting independent action. Recognize this as an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
Abu Yusuf's view is based on practical necessity.
3
Apply the fatwa of Imam Isma'il al-Zahid
The passage from al-Khaniyya presents a scenario: two qayyims appointed by judges of different towns. Imam Isma'il al-Zahid rules that each may act independently. Understand that this is an exception allowed by later scholars.
The fatwa also says a judge may remove the other judge's appointee if beneficial.
4
Handle the hiring prohibition
The text asks: can one nazhir hire the other? The answer is no, analogizing to co-executors (wasiyyan) where one cannot sell to the other. Know that this ruling follows from the default rule of joint action.
Nazhir is either like a wasi (executor) or an agent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس لأحد الناظرين التصرف دون الآخر عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف. وفي الخانية: ولو أن قيمين في وقف أقام كل قيم قاضي بلدة غير قاضي بلدة أخرى هل يجوز لكل واحد منهما أن يتصرف بدون الآخر؟ قال الشيخ الإمام إسماعيل الزاهد ينبغي أن يجوز تصرف كل واحد منهما، ولو أن واحداً من هذين القاضيين أراد أن يعزل القيم الذي أقامه القاضي الآخر فإن رأى القاضي المصلحة في عزل الآخر كان له ذلك وإلا فلا .اهـ وفيه دليل على أن للقاضي عزل منصوب قاض آخر بغير خيانة إذا رأى المصلحة .اهـ. فإن قلت: هل لأحد الناظرين أن يؤجر الآخر؟ قلت: لا يجوز لما في الخانية من كتاب الوصايا : لو باع أحد الوصيين لصاحبه شيئاً من التركة لا يجوز عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد لأن عندهما لا ينفرد أحد الوصيين بالتصرف والناظر إما وصي أو كيل.
And it is not permissible for one of the two overseers (nazirs) to act without the other according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf. And in al-Khaniyya: 'If there are two qayyims in a waqf, each appointed by the judge of a different town, is it permissible for each to act without the other?' Sheikh Imam Isma'il al-Zahid said: 'It should be permissible for each to act. And if one of these two judges wishes to remove the qayyim appointed by the other judge, if the judge sees benefit in removing the other, he may do so, otherwise not.' End. In it is evidence that a judge may remove the appointee of another judge without treachery if he sees benefit. Then if you ask: 'Is it permissible for one of the two nazirs to hire the other?' I say: 'No, because in al-Khaniyya in the book of wills: If one of two executors sells something from the estate to his co-executor, it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because in their view one executor may not act alone. And the nazir is either an executor or an agent.'
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. The default position ('indahuma) of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani is that one of two co-nazhirs (overseers of a waqf) cannot act independently; they must act jointly. Abu Yusuf disagreed. However, a later fatwa from Imam Isma'il al-Zahid, cited in al-Khaniyya, permits each qayyim to act alone if they were appointed by judges from different towns, provided there is no conflict of interest. This is a relaxation based on practical necessity. The passage further clarifies that a judge may remove the appointee of another judge if it serves the public interest, even without proven treachery. Finally, it addresses the specific question: can one nazhir hire the other? The answer is no, analogizing to the case of co-executors (wasiyyan) where one cannot sell to the other, because acting alone is prohibited in such matters. The nazhir is either like a wasi (executor) or a wakeel (agent), so similar rules apply.

Key Terms
الناظر (al-nāẓir): The overseer or custodian of a waqf, responsible for its management.
القيم (al-qayyim): Synonym for nazhir; custodian of waqf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, can one nazhir hire the other?
A) Yes, because hiring is different from selling.
B) No, by analogy to co-executors who cannot sell to each other.
C) Yes, if both consent.
D) Only if the other nazhir is absent.

Key Takeaway
Co-nazhirs must act jointly by default, but a later fatwa allows independent action when appointed by different judges; one nazhir cannot hire the other.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
6 min
Following the Guarantor in Waqf Usurpation
Ruling on liability priority in waqf usurpation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling on which usurper the mutawalli should pursue to benefit the waqf, and identify when the other is discharged.

Core Idea
The mutawalli must follow the more solvent usurper to maximize benefit to the waqf, just as an owner would.

When waqf property is usurped, the mutawalli (trustee) may have recourse against multiple wrongdoers. This rule clarifies the priority: follow the one whose liability is most beneficial for the endowment, discharging the other.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
The mutawalli has a claim for property worth two thousand dirhams against two successive usurpers.
2
Identify the rule
The mutawalli should follow the second usurper if he is solvent, because holding the second liable is more beneficial (anfa') for the waqf.
An alternative view makes real estate liable through usurpation; the ruling adapts accordingly.
3
Apply the exception
If the first usurper is more solvent, follow him instead, because that is more beneficial.
4
Note the consequence
When the mutawalli follows one, the other is discharged, similar to an owner choosing which usurper to hold liable.
This is analogous to the owner's right in general property law.

Source Text

الانفاق
أن يحاسب أمناءه فيما في أيديهم من أموال اليتامى ليعرف الخائن فيستبدله، وكذا القوام على الأوقاف ويقبل قولهم في مقدار ما حصل في أيديهم من مقدار الغلات الوصي والقيم فيه سواء. والأصل فيه أن القول قول القابض في مقدار المقبوض وفيما يخبر من الانفاق على اليتيم أو على الضيعة ومؤنات الأراضي. وفي أدب القاضي للخصاف: ويقبل قول الوصي في المحتمل دون القيم لأن الوصي من فوض إليه الحفظ والتصرف والقيم من فوض إليه الحفظ دون التصرف، وكثير من مشايخنا سووا بين الوصي والقيم فيما لا بد فيه من وقالوا: ويقبل قولهما فيه وقاسوه على قيم المسجد أو واحد من أهل المحلة إذا اشترى للمسجد ما لا بد منه كالحصير والحشيش والدهن وأجر الخادم ونحوه لا يضمن للإذن دلالة ولا يتعطل المسجد كذا هذا وبه يفتي في زماننا قال رضي الله عنه : والصحيح والصواب في عرفنا بخوارزم هذا أنه لا فرق بينهما. (ط) وإن اتهمه القاضي يحلفه وإن كان أميناً كالمودع يدعي هلاك الوديعة أو ردها قيل إنما يستحلف إذا ادعى عليه شيئاً معلوماً، وقيل يحلف على كل حال وإن أخبروا أنهم أنفقوا على اليتيم والضيعة من إنزال الأرض كذا وبقي في أيدينا كذا، فإن عرف بالأمانة يقبل القاضي الإجمال ولا يجبره على التفسير شيئاً فشيئاً، وإن كان متهماً يجبره القاضي على التفسير شيئاً فشيئاً ولا يحبسه ولكن يحضره يومين أو ثلاثة أو يخوفه ويهدده إن لم يفسره، فإن فعل وإلا يكتفي منه باليمين ولو عزل القاضي ونصب غيره فقال الوصي للمنصوب حاسبني المعزول لا يقبل منه إلا ببينة وفي وقف الناصحي إذا أجر الواقف أو قيمه أو وصيه أو أمينه ثم قال قبضت الغلة فضاعت أو فرقته على الموقوف عليهم وأنكروا فالقول له مع يمينه . اهـ ما في القنية فقد علمت أن مشروعية المحاسبات للنظار إنما هي ليعرف القاضي الخائن من الأمين لا لأخذ شيء من النظار للقاضي واتباعه، والواقع بالقاهرة في زماننا الثاني وقد شاهدنا فيها من الفساد للأوقاف كثيراً بحيث يقدم كلفة المحاسبة على العمارة والمستحقين، وكل ذلك من علامات الساعة المصدقة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام كما رواه البخاري في أول كتاب العلم إذا وسد الأمر لغير أهله فانتظروا الساعة»(۱) بمتولي المسجد إذا أخذ غلات المسجد ومات من غير بيان .اهـ. أقول : أما إذا كانت الغلة مستحقة لقوم بالشرط فيضمن مطلقاً ثم ذكر الاستدلال عليه فراجعه قلت ويؤيده قولهم إن غلة الوقف يملكها الموقوف عليه وإن لم يقبل وما سيأتي في باب دعوى الرجلين من أن دعوی من قبيل دعوى الملك المطلق، وحينئذ فتكون في حكم سائر الأمانات فتنقلب مضمونة بالموت عن تجهيل كشريك ومفاوض والله أعلم. قوله : ( وفي وقف الناصحي الخ قال الرملي: سئل مولانا شيخ (۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب العلم باب ٢.
الغلة
Book of Waqf. Liability: Property equal to two thousand dirhams, then the trustee follows the second usurper if he is solvent, according to the view that makes real estate liable through usurpation, because holding the second liable is more beneficial for the endowment. If the first is more solvent than the second, he follows the first, because holding the first liable is more beneficial for the endowment. If the trustee follows one of them, the other is discharged, just as if the owner chooses to hold the first or second usurper liable, the other is discharged. End. Among them: A tenant farmer (akar) took from the endowment and the trustee settled with him for something; if the farmer is rich, it is not permissible to reduce from the endowment property; if the farmer is poor, that is permissible. End. It is interpreted as referring to when the endowment is for the poor, as he restricted it, regarding when a poor person lives in the endowment house and the trustee waives the rent for him. But if it is for known beneficiaries and specific entitled persons, it is not permissible to waive or reduce through settlement absolutely. On this basis, it is not permissible to lease for less than the fair rent with a significant loss from a poor person if the endowment is for specific individuals, but if it is an endowment for the poor, it is permissible. In al-Is'af: And if he bought a garment with his mule and gave it to the poor, he is liable for what he paid from the endowment property because the purchase was for him. A wall between two houses, one being an endowment and the other private property, it collapsed and the owner of the property built it within the boundary of the endowment house. Abu al-Qasim said: The trustee raises the matter to the judge to compel him to demolish it, then build it where it was originally. And if the trustee says to the builder: I will give you the value of the construction and let it stay where you built, and you build another wall for yourself on your boundary, Abu al-Qasim said: The trustee does not have that; rather, he orders him to demolish it and build it where it was originally. End. And if the trustee of the endowment takes something from its produce and then dies without explanation, he is not liable; thus they said. Al-Tarsusi in Anfa' al-Wasa'il restricted it as a research: if the beneficiary did not demand, but if the beneficiary demanded and he did not pay and then died without explanation, then he is liable. End. Its implication is that if he claimed during his lifetime that it perished, his statement is not accepted, because he became liable by preventing the beneficiary after demand. In al-Qunyah: And it is appropriate for the judge... (a dispute about sowing). His statement: (And al-Tarsusi restricted it...) The text of his wording: The detail should be that if the beneficiaries demanded the money from him and he delayed and then died without specifying, then he is liable. And if there was no demand from them and he died without specification, then it should also be said that if he was praiseworthy among the people, known for religiosity and trustworthiness, then there is no liability. And if he was not like that and time passed with the money in his hand and he did not distribute it and there was no legal impediment, then he is liable. End. And his statement that the detail should be from the copy of al-Ramli, he objected to the author that it does not match what he transmitted from him. Then he said: Acting on their absolute statements is determined, and no regard is given to what al-Tarsusi said as a research; the impediment's possibility is sufficient. And it has been said about al-Tarsusi that he is not among the scholars of fiqh, and the one who said that is al-Kamal ibn al-Humam, may Allah have mercy on him. End. Reflect. Then know that al-Bayri in Sharh al-Ashbah mentioned that his statement 'produce of the endowment' occurred absolutely in al-Walwaljiyyah and al-Bazzaziyyah, and Qadikhan restricted it. [Missing text] Book of Waqf. Spending: That he should audit his trustees regarding what is in their hands of orphans' property to know the treacherous one and replace him, and similarly the supervisors of endowments, and their statement is accepted regarding the amount that came into their hands from the amount of produce. The executor and the caretaker are the same in this. The principle is that the statement of the holder is accepted regarding the amount received and regarding what he reports of spending on the orphan or on the estate and expenses of lands. In Adab al-Qadi by al-Khassaf: The statement of the executor is accepted in what is plausible, but not the caretaker, because the executor is delegated with preservation and disposal, while the caretaker is delegated with preservation without disposal. Many of our shaykhs equated the executor and the caretaker in what is indispensable and said: Their statement is accepted in it, and they analogized it to the caretaker of a mosque or one of the neighborhood residents if he buys for the mosque what is indispensable, like a mat, grass, oil, wages of a servant, etc.; he is not liable because of implicit permission and the mosque should not be left idle; similarly this, and according to this fatwa is given in our time. He said, may Allah be pleased with him: The correct and proper in our custom in Khwarazm is that there is no difference between them. (T) And if the judge suspects him, he swears him, even if he is trustworthy, like a depositary who claims loss of the deposit or return. It is said that he is only sworn if a known thing is claimed against him. And it is said he is sworn in any case. And if they report that they spent on the orphan and the estate from the produce of the land such and such and in our hands remains such, if he is known for trustworthiness, the judge accepts the summary and does not compel him to detail it item by item. And if he is suspected, the judge compels him to detail it item by item, and does not imprison him, but summons him for two or three days, or threatens and intimidates him if he does not detail it. If he does, otherwise he suffices with an oath. And if the judge is removed and another appointed, and the executor says to the appointed: The removed one settled accounts with me, it is not accepted from him except with evidence. And in Waqf al-Nasihi: If the founder or his caretaker or executor or trustee leases, then says I received the produce and it was lost or I distributed it to the beneficiaries and they deny, then his statement is accepted with his oath. End of what is in al-Qunyah. So you know that the legislation of audits for supervisors is only for the judge to know the treacherous from the trustworthy, not to take anything from the supervisors for the judge and his followers. The reality in Cairo in our time is the second; we have witnessed much corruption of endowments therein, such that the expense of accounting is given priority over building and beneficiaries. All of that is from the signs of the hour, confirming his saying, peace be upon him, as narrated by al-Bukhari in the beginning of Kitab al-Ilm: 'When a matter is entrusted to other than its people, then await the Hour' regarding the trustee of a mosque if he takes the mosque's produce and dies without explanation. End. I say: As for when the produce is due to a people by condition, he is liable absolutely. Then he mentioned the evidence for it, so refer to it. I said: And it is supported by their statement that the produce of an endowment is owned by the beneficiary even if not accepted, and what will come in the chapter on the claim of two men, that such a claim is like a claim of absolute ownership. Thus it is in the ruling of other trusts, so it becomes liable through death without specification, like a partner and a participant. And Allah knows best. His statement: (And in Waqf al-Nasihi…) al-Ramli said: Our master Shaykh was asked…
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, presenting multiple rulings related to waqf (endowment). The author, Ibn Nujaym, addresses the liability of the mutawalli (trustee) and procedures. The passage begins with a ruling on following a guarantor (ضمان) in case of usurpation, stating that the trustee should pursue the more beneficial option for the endowment. Then comes a ruling about a tenant farmer (أكار) who takes from the endowment: if the farmer is rich, a settlement reducing the endowment's property is not allowed; if poor, it is allowed, but this is restricted to endowments for the poor. For endowments with specified beneficiaries, no reduction is permitted. Next is a ruling about a collapsed wall between an endowment house and a private house: the private owner who rebuilds on endowment land must demolish and rebuild on his own land; the trustee cannot accept compensation. Then a ruling on a mutawalli who takes produce and dies without explanation: generally not liable unless the beneficiary demanded payment. Al-Tarsusi's detailed view is discussed, and al-Ramli criticizes it, upholding the absolute view. The passage then discusses accounting procedures: the judge should audit trustees to identify the treacherous, accepting their statements in plausible matters. A distinction between an executor (وصي) and a caretaker (قيم) is noted from al-Khassaf: the executor's word is accepted in plausible matters, but not the caretaker's, though many later scholars equated them, and fatwa is given accordingly. Finally, a ruling from Waqf al-Nasihi: if the founder or his agent claims to have received and distributed produce, his word is accepted with oath. The author comments on the corruption of audits in his time. Throughout, the Hanafi school's positions are presented with details and differences.

Key Terms
الضمان (al-ḍamān): Liability, especially financial responsibility for usurped waqf property.
المتولي (al-mutawallī): The trustee of the waqf, responsible for its administration.
القيم (al-qayyim): Used synonymously with mutawalli here; a caretaker.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a waqf property is usurped by two persons, who should the mutawalli pursue according to the passage?
A) Always the first usurper
B) Always the second usurper
C) The more solvent usurper
D) Both simultaneously

Key Takeaway
The mutawalli must prioritize the most beneficial recovery for the waqf, following the solvent usurper.

Waqf — Endowment
intermediate
6 min
Settlement with a Poor Tenant Farmer in Waqf
Ruling on settlement and reduction for tenant farmers in waqf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when a settlement reducing waqf property is allowed based on the farmer's financial status and the waqf's beneficiaries.

Core Idea
Reducing rent for a poor farmer is allowed only if the waqf is for the poor; otherwise, no reduction is permitted.

A tenant farmer (akar) who took from the waqf may settle with the mutawalli. This lesson clarifies the permissible conditions: if the farmer is poor and the waqf is for the poor, reduction is allowed; otherwise, it is prohibited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actor and action
An akar (tenant farmer) took something from the waqf, and the mutawalli makes a settlement involving a reduction.
2
Check the farmer's wealth
If the farmer is rich (ghani), reduction is not allowed; if poor, it may be allowed.
3
Check the waqf's beneficiaries
The ruling is interpreted as applying when the waqf is for the poor (fuqara). If the waqf is for specific named beneficiaries, no reduction is allowed even if the farmer is poor.
4
Derive the consequence
Leasing below fair rent with a significant loss is prohibited for specific beneficiaries, but allowed for a waqf for the poor.
The text also mentions buying a garment with waqf produce and giving to poor: that is not allowed as it is a personal purchase.
